Exceptions to Joint Action in Agency
Lists five cases where one agent may act alone

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five exceptional cases where one agent may act alone and explain the underlying rationale of no need for deliberation.

Core Idea
Where no deliberation is needed, one agent suffices.

In Hanafi agency law, when a principal appoints two agents, the default rule is that both must act jointly. However, certain tasks are purely executory—they involve merely conveying the principal's words or performing a necessary duty without independent judgment. This lesson examines the five specific exceptions where one agent alone can validly perform the task.

Guided Path
1
Recall the general rule
The default in Hanafi wakalah is that two agents must act jointly unless the principal allowed separate action.
This rule ensures deliberation when tasks require judgment.
2
List the five exceptions from the passage
They are: litigation, divorcing a wife without compensation, emancipating a slave without compensation, returning a trust, and paying a debt.
3
Identify the common feature
All exceptions share the absence of need for ra'y (opinion or deliberation); they are executory or obligatory.
The agent merely transmits the principal’s intention or performs a required act.
4
Understand the rationale for each
Litigation: both agents speaking causes disorder. Divorce/emancipation without compensation: no negotiation, just conveying words. Trust/debt: acts that must be done anyway.
The key phrase is 'bighayr 'iwad' (without compensation) for divorce and emancipation.
5
Note the boundary case
If the principal says 'if you wish, both may divorce,' discretion is introduced, so both agents are required.
This shows that the exceptions apply only when the agent has no discretionary power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ ۱۳۹۱ (۲۲) الا ان يوكلهما بالخصومة او بطلاق زوجته بغير عوض او بعتق عبده بغیر عوض او برد وديعة عنده او بقضاء دين عليه
یہاں پانچ مثالیں دی ہیں ان سب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جن کاموں میں رائے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے صرف موکل کی بات پیش کرنا ہے ان میں اگر دو آدمیوں کو وکیل بنایا اور ایک وکیل نے کام کر لیا تب بھی درست ہو جائے گا۔ مثلا اگر خصومت کے لئے دو آدمیوں کو وکیل بنایا اور دونوں مجلس قضاء میں بولنے لگیں تو شور ہو گا اور آداب مجلس کے خلاف ہے۔ اس لئے ایک وکیل کا بولنا کافی ہے۔ اسی طرح بغیر عوض کے بیوی کو طلاق دینا ہے تو چونکہ عوض نہیں لینا صرف شوہر کی بات کو نقل کرنا ہے جس سے طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ اس لئے اس میں دوسرے وکیل کے مشورے کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں اس لئے ایک ہی وکیل کام کر لے تو درست ہے۔ بغیر عوض کے غلام آزاد کرنے میں بھی یہی حال ہے۔ اپنے پاس کسی کی امانت ہے اس کو واپس بہر حال کرنا ہے اس لئے دوسرے وکیل کی رائے کی ضرورت نہیں۔ یا قرض ادا کرنا ہے جو بہر حال کرنا ہی ہے اس لئے دوسرے وکیل کے مشورے کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے ایک وکیل کر دے تو درست ہو جائے گا۔ اگر یوں کہا کہ اگر چاہو تو تم دونوں وکیل طلاق دیدو تو چونکہ یہاں رائے کی ضرورت ہے اس لئے دونوں وکیلوں کی ضرورت ہوگی۔
(1391) (22) Unless he appoints them for litigation, or for divorcing his wife without compensation, or for emancipating his slave without compensation, or for returning a trust that is with him, or for paying a debt that is upon him. Here five examples are given. The gist of all is that in tasks that do not require opinion but only conveying the principal's words, if two people are appointed as agents and one agent does the task, it will still be valid. For example, if two people are appointed as agents for litigation and both speak in the court, it would be disruptive and contrary to court etiquette, so one agent speaking is sufficient. Similarly, divorcing a wife without compensation is merely conveying the husband's words by which divorce occurs, so the other agent's consultation is not needed; thus one agent doing it is valid. The same applies to emancipating a slave without compensation. Returning a trust must be done anyway, so the other agent's opinion is not needed. Paying a debt must be done anyway, so the other agent's consultation is not needed; thus one agent doing it is valid. If the principal says 'If you wish, you both may divorce,' then since here opinion is required, both agents are needed.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage lists five exceptions to the general rule that two agents must act jointly. The common feature is that these tasks do not require independent judgment (ra'y) but are purely executory: conveying words (litigation, divorce, emancipation) or performing a necessary duty (returning a trust, paying a debt). In litigation, having both agents speak would cause disorder in court, so one suffices. In divorce and emancipation without compensation, the agent merely transmits the principal's declaration; no deliberation is needed. Returning a trust and paying a debt are obligations that must be fulfilled regardless of opinion. The commentary adds an important nuance: if the principal says 'if you wish, both may divorce,' then opinion is required because the agents have discretion, so both must act together.

Key Terms
خصومة (khusumah): Litigation; legal dispute in court.
بغير عوض (bighayr 'iwad): Without compensation; gratuitous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT among the five exceptions where one agent can act alone?
A) Litigation
B) Divorce with compensation
C) Emancipating a slave without compensation
D) Returning a trust

Key Takeaway
One agent may act alone in executory tasks—litigation, gratuitous divorce, gratuitous emancipation, returning a trust, and paying a debt—because they require no deliberation.

Sub-Agency Requires Principal's Permission
Ruling statement prohibiting sub-agency without permission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an agent appointing a sub-agent and identify the two forms of permission that make it valid.

Core Idea
An agent cannot delegate his authority unless the principal explicitly permits or says 'act on your opinion.'

This passage from al-Sharh al-Samari establishes a fundamental rule of agency (wakalah): the agent's authority is personal. He cannot pass it to another without the principal's consent. The reason is that the principal chose the agent for his specific judgment and trust. We will examine the ruling, its exceptions, and the legal effect of a sub-agent when appointed with permission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the agent appointing another agent for the same task. The ruling is that it is not permissible without permission.
The Arabic 'laysa' indicates a prohibition close to haram.
2
Recognize the exceptions
Two forms of permission from the principal allow delegation: explicit permission, or a general authorization like 'act according to your opinion.'
The phrase 'i'mal bi-ra'yik' gives full discretion including delegation.
3
Understand the change in relationship
If a sub-agent is appointed with permission, he becomes the agent of the original principal directly, not the first agent's agent.
This means the principal can hold the sub-agent accountable directly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۳۹۲] (۲۳) وليس للوكيل ان يوكل فيما وكل به الا ان يأذن له الموكل او يقول له اعمل برأيك
جس کام کا موکل نے وکیل بنایا ہے۔ وکیل چاہے کہ اس کام کا وکیل کسی دوسرے کو بنا دے ایسا نہیں کرسکتا۔ ہاں ! موکل دوسرے کو وکیل بنانے کی اجازت دیدے یا یوں کہے کہ آپ اپنی صواب دید کے مطابق کام کر سکتے ہیں تو وہ دوسرے کو وکیل بنا سکتے ہیں۔ موکل نے وکیل کی رائے پر اعتماد کیا ہے۔ وکیل کے وکیل کی رائے پر اعتماد نہیں کیا ہے اس لئے وہ وکیل نہیں بنا سکتا (۲) قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ جو عہدہ آپ کو سپرد کیا ہے وہ بغیر اجازت کے کسی اور کو سپرد نہیں کر سکتے ۔ ہاں ! اجازت دیدے تو وکیل بنا سکتا ہے۔ لیکن بعد میں وہ وکیل خود اصل موکل کا وکیل ہوگا وکیل کا وکیل نہیں ہو گا۔
(1392) (23) And it is not for the agent to appoint another agent in that which he was appointed as agent, unless the principal permits him or says to him 'Act according to your opinion.' The agent cannot appoint another person as agent for the task for which the principal appointed him. However, if the principal gives permission to appoint another agent, or says 'You may act according to your discretion,' then he can appoint another agent. The principal has relied on the agent's opinion, not on the opinion of the agent's agent, so he cannot appoint an agent. The rule is that the office entrusted to you cannot be entrusted to another without permission. However, if permission is given, he can appoint an agent. But afterwards, that agent will be the agent of the original principal, not the agent of the agent.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage states a key principle of agency: the agent cannot delegate his authority to another without explicit permission from the principal. The reason is that the principal trusts the agent's personal judgment and skills, not that of a stranger. Two forms of permission are allowed: explicit permission to appoint a sub-agent, or a general authorization to act according to his own discretion (i'ml bi-ra'yik). The commentary also clarifies that if a sub-agent is appointed with permission, he becomes the agent of the original principal directly, not the agent of the first agent. This means the principal can hold the sub-agent accountable directly.

Key Terms
يوكّل (yuwakkil): To appoint as an agent; the verb form used for the agent appointing a sub-agent.
اعمل برأيك (i'mal bi-ra'yik): Act according to your opinion; a general authorization that permits delegation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a principal says to his agent 'Act according to your opinion,' can the agent appoint a sub-agent?
A) Yes
B) No
C) Only if the sub-agent is a relative
D) Only after informing the principal

Key Takeaway
An agent cannot delegate his authority without the principal's permission, but if permission is given (explicitly or by 'act on opinion'), the sub-agent becomes the principal's agent directly.

Sub-Agent's Contract Approved After Absence
Ruling on subsequent approval of sub-agent's contract done in absence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sub-agent's contract made without the first agent's presence and explain how subsequent approval validates it.

Core Idea
A sub-agent's unauthorized act becomes valid if the first agent later approves it.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from agency law: a first agent appoints a sub-agent without the principal's permission, and the sub-agent performs an act in the first agent's absence. Initially, the act is not valid because it lacks the first agent's involvement. However, the Hanafi school holds that the first agent's subsequent approval (ijazah) retroactively validates the act. This principle of ratification is similar to curing defects in contracts through later consent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their roles
There are three parties: the principal (who appointed the first agent), the first agent (who appointed the sub-agent without principal's permission), and the sub-agent (who acted in the absence of the first agent).
The sub-agent's appointment itself is valid but the sub-agent's act is initially incomplete.
2
Recognize the initial invalidity
The sub-agent's contract made in the first agent's absence is not valid because the first agent's judgment and authority were not present at the time of the act.
The act is not void (batil) but rather suspended or ineffective until ratified.
3
Identify the validating act
When the first agent subsequently approves (ajazahu) the sub-agent's act, this approval retroactively validates the contract. The act becomes jā'iz (valid and effective).
Approval must be explicit or implied; silence without objection may also indicate approval.
4
State the final ruling
The Hanafi ruling: the sub-agent's contract, made in the absence of the first agent, becomes valid upon the first agent's subsequent approval. This is a sahih (valid) contract from the moment of approval, as if the first agent had authorized it at the time.
This ruling is based on the principle that subsequent consent can cure a prior unauthorized act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ ۱۳۹۴ (۲۵) وان عقد بغير حضرته فاجازه الوكيل الاول جاز
وکیل نے بغیر موکل کی اجازت کے وکیل بنایا تھا پھر اس نے وکیل اول کی غیر موجودگی میں کام انجام دیا پھر وکیل اول نے اس کو پسند کیا اور اجازت دیدی تب بھی جائے ہو گیا۔
(1394) (25) And if he contracted in his absence, and the first agent approved it, it is valid. The agent had appointed a sub-agent without the principal's permission, then the sub-agent performed the task in the absence of the first agent, then the first agent approved it and gave permission, then it became valid.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where the sub-agent acts in the first agent's absence. Initially, the action is not valid because the first agent's judgment was not included. However, if the first agent subsequently approves (ijazah) the sub-agent's action, it becomes valid. The approval retroactively confirms the action, similar to ratification in contract law. This is based on the principle that subsequent consent validates a prior unauthorized act.

Key Terms
أجازه (ajazahu): He approved it; subsequent ratification of a prior unauthorized act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What makes a sub-agent's contract valid when it was made in the absence of the first agent?
A) The sub-agent's good faith
B) The first agent's subsequent approval
C) The principal's later permission
D) The presence of witnesses

Key Takeaway
A sub-agent's unauthorized act performed in the first agent's absence becomes valid upon the first agent's subsequent approval, based on the principle of ratification.

Agent Cannot Sub-delegate Without Permission
Ruling on sub-delegation in agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an agent appointing a sub-agent and identify the conditions under which it becomes permissible.

Core Idea
An agent cannot delegate his task without the principal's explicit permission—agency is built on personal trust, not transferable.

Agency in Hanafi fiqh is a fiduciary relationship based on personal trust. The principal chooses a specific agent for his reliability. This lesson explains why the agent cannot simply pass that responsibility to another person without the principal's consent, and when such delegation becomes valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Locate the statement: 'It is not permissible for the agent to appoint another agent...' Understand that the default ruling is prohibition (haram).
2
Find the exceptions
The text provides two conditions that make sub-delegation permissible: explicit permission from the principal, or the principal's instruction to 'act according to your discretion.'
3
Understand the rationale
The commentary explains that the principal relied on the agent's judgment, not on the judgment of a third party. This trust cannot be transferred without approval.
This is a key principle of Hanafi agency law.
4
Note the legal consequence
If the agent sub-delegates without permission, the act is invalid and the principal can reject it. If permission is given, the sub-agent becomes the agent of the principal, not of the first agent.
5
Apply to a scenario
Consider a case where A appoints B to sell his car. B cannot ask C to handle the sale unless A says 'go ahead' or 'use your own judgment.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس للوكيل ان يوكل فيما وكل به الا ان يأذن له الموكل او يقول له اعمل برأيك [۱۳۹۲] (۲۳) وکیل کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ اس کام میں دوسرے کو وکیل بنائے جس میں اس کو وکیل بنایا ہے مگر یہ کہ اجازت دیدے موکل یا اس کو موکل کہہ دے کہ اپنی صواب دید کے مطابق کریں۔ جس کام کا موکل نے وکیل بنایا ہے۔ وکیل چاہے کہ اس کام کا وکیل کسی دوسرے کو بنا دے ایسا نہیں کرسکتا۔ ہاں ! موکل دوسرے کو وکیل بنانے کی اجازت دیدے یا یوں کہے کہ آپ اپنی صواب دید کے مطابق کام کر سکتے ہیں تو وہ دوسرے کو وکیل بنا سکتے ہیں۔ موکل نے وکیل کی رائے پر اعتماد کیا ہے۔ وکیل کے وکیل کی رائے پر اعتماد نہیں کیا ہے اس لئے وہ وکیل نہیں بنا سکتا (۲) قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ جو عہدہ آپ کو سپرد کیا ہے وہ بغیر اجازت کے کسی اور کو سپرد نہیں کر سکتے ۔ ہاں ! اجازت دیدے تو وکیل بنا سکتا ہے۔ لیکن بعد میں وہ وکیل خود اصل موکل کا وکیل ہوگا وکیل کا وکیل نہیں ہو گا۔
It is not permissible for the agent to appoint another agent in that which he was appointed, unless the principal permits him or says, 'Act according to your discretion.' [1392] (23) It is not permissible for the agent to appoint another person for the task for which he was appointed, unless the principal gives permission or says, 'Act according to your discretion.' The agent cannot appoint another for the task the principal assigned to him. Yes, if the principal permits appointing another or says, 'You may act according to your discretion,' then he can appoint another. The principal relied on the agent's opinion, not on the sub-agent's opinion, so he cannot appoint a sub-agent. The rule is that a position entrusted to you cannot be entrusted to another without permission. Yes, if permission is given, he can appoint, but then that sub-agent becomes the agent of the principal, not of the first agent.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Book of Agency. The matn states that an agent (wakil) is not allowed to delegate the task to another person (tawkil) unless the principal (muwakkil) explicitly permits it or tells him to act on his own discretion. The commentary explains the reason: the principal placed trust in the agent's judgment, not in the judgment of some unknown person. Therefore, without explicit permission, the agent cannot appoint a sub-agent. However, if the principal grants permission, the sub-agent's appointment is valid, but legally the sub-agent becomes the agent of the principal, not of the first agent. This is based on the Hanafi principle that agency is a fiduciary relationship based on personal trust.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakīl): Agent appointed by the principal to perform a specific task on his behalf.
موكل (muwakkil): Principal who appoints the agent.
توكيل (tawkīl): The act of the agent appointing a sub-agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When can a Hanafi agent appoint a sub-agent?
A) Whenever he needs help
B) Only if the principal gives permission or says 'act on your discretion'
C) Only with the consent of the judge
D) If the task is too difficult for him alone

Key Takeaway
An agent in Hanafi fiqh cannot sub-delegate without the principal's permission; the relationship is personal and based on trust.

Sub-agent's Contract in Agent's Presence
Ruling on validity of sub-agent's contract in presence of first agent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sub-agent's contract made without the principal's permission and identify the condition that validates it.

Core Idea
A sub-agent's contract is valid if made in the first agent's presence, because the agent's judgment is thereby included.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi principle in agency (wakala): when an agent appoints a sub-agent without the principal's authorization, the sub-agent's actions are generally void. However, an exception arises if the sub-agent acts in the physical presence of the first agent. Understanding this exception requires grasping the purpose of agency: the principal hires the agent for his judgment (ra'y). When the first agent is present, his judgment is effectively incorporated into the sub-agent's act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
The act: an agent appoints a sub-agent without the principal's permission. The default Hanafi ruling is that such sub-agency is invalid.
2
State the exception
If the sub-agent contracts in the presence of the first agent, the contract becomes valid (jā'iz).
3
Understand the rationale (ra'y)
The principal hired the first agent for his judgment (ra'y). When the first agent is present, his judgment is considered to be included in the sub-agent's action, fulfilling the purpose of agency.
4
Reformulate the principle
The underlying principle is that the inclusion of the first agent's opinion suffices to validate the sub-agent's act.
5
Contrast with absence
If the first agent is absent during the sub-agent's action, the contract would be invalid without the principal's explicit permission, because the judgment is not included.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان وكل بغير اذن موكله فعقد وكيله بحضرته جاز [۱۳۹۳] (۲۴) پس اگر موکل کی اجازت کے بغیر وکیل بنایا، پس اس کے وکیل نے اس کے سامنے عقد کیا تو جائز ہے۔ وکیل نے موکل کی اجازت کے بغیر وکیل بنا دیا۔ پھر دوسرے وکیل نے پہلے وکیل کے سامنے وہ کام کیا تو درست ہو جائے گا۔ وکیل بنانے میں اصل مقصود رائے ہے۔ پس جب دوسرے وکیل نے پہلے وکیل کی موجودگی میں کام کیا تو پہلے وکیل کی رائے اس کام میں شامل ہو گئی۔ اس لئے دوسرے وکیل کا کام کرنا درست ہے۔ گویا کہ پہلے ہی وکیل نے کام انجام دیا۔ اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ وکیل اول کی رائے شامل ہونا کافی ہے۔
If he appoints [a sub-agent] without the permission of his principal, and his [sub-]agent contracts in his presence, it is valid. [1393] (24) So if he appoints a sub-agent without the principal's permission, then that sub-agent makes a contract in his presence, it is valid. The agent appointed a sub-agent without the principal's permission. Then the sub-agent performed the task in the presence of the first agent. It will be valid. The main purpose in appointing an agent is opinion/judgment. So when the sub-agent acts in the presence of the first agent, the opinion of the first agent is included in that act. Therefore, the sub-agent's act is correct, as if the first agent himself performed the task. The principle is that the inclusion of the first agent's opinion is sufficient.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This ruling addresses a scenario where an agent (the first wakil) appoints a sub-agent without the principal's permission. If the sub-agent then performs the task (e.g., makes a contract) in the physical presence of the first agent, the contract is valid. The reason given in the commentary is that the primary purpose of appointing an agent is to utilize his judgment (ra'y). Since the first agent is present, his judgment is effectively incorporated into the sub-agent's action. Thus, it is as if the first agent himself acted. The underlying Hanafi principle is that the presence and implicit approval of the first agent suffices to validate the sub-agent's act, even without the principal's explicit permission.

Key Terms
حضرة (Hadrat): The presence of the first agent; the sub-agent acts in his presence.
رائے (ra'y): Opinion or judgment; the principal hired the agent for his judgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this text, when is a sub-agent's contract valid without the principal's permission?
A) Only if the principal later ratifies it
B) If the sub-agent is a relative of the principal
C) If the sub-agent acts in the presence of the first agent
D) If the task is urgent

Key Takeaway
The presence of the first agent during the sub-agent's act validates the contract, as the agent's judgment is thereby included.

Sub-agent's Contract Validated by Later Ratification
Ruling on validity of sub-agent's contract made in absence and then ratified

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a sub-agent's contract made in the first agent's absence becomes valid upon the first agent's subsequent ratification.

Core Idea
A sub-agent's contract made without the first agent's presence is validated by the first agent's later ratification.

This lesson examines a case where a sub-agent acts in the absence of the first agent. Initially, the act would be invalid because the first agent's judgment was absent. However, Hanafi fiqh allows the first agent's subsequent approval (ijāza) to cure this defect. Understanding this principle is important for agency contracts where ratification can retroactively validate an act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The sub-agent performs an act (e.g., enters a contract) without the first agent being present. The first agent had previously appointed the sub-agent without the principal's permission.
The act occurs in the absence of both the principal and the first agent.
2
Note the initial defect
Because the first agent's opinion was not included at the time of the act, the contract is initially invalid. The first agent's presence and consent are essential for the sub-agent's authority.
The defect is the absence of the first agent's supervision.
3
Recognize the cure by ratification
If the first agent later expresses approval or grants permission (ijāza), this ratification retroactively validates the act. The first agent's opinion is now included, fulfilling the purpose of agency.
Ratification can be explicit or implicit (e.g., by conduct).
4
State the final ruling
After ratification, the contract becomes valid (jā'iz). The sub-agent's act is now legally binding as if the first agent had been present.
This ruling is specific to Hanafi fiqh; other schools may differ.

Source Text

وان عقد بغير حضرته فاجازه الوكيل الاول جاز [۱۳۹۴] (۲۵) وکیل نے بغیر موکل کی اجازت کے وکیل بنایا تھا پھر اس نے وکیل اول کی غیر موجودگی میں کام انجام دیا پھر وکیل اول نے اس کو پسند کیا اور اجازت دیدی تب بھی جائز ہو گیا۔ وکیل اول کی رائے شامل ہونا اصل تھی وہ ہو گئی اس لئے اس کا کام کرنا جائز ہو گیا۔
And if he contracts in his absence, and the first agent approves it, it is valid. [1394] (25) The agent had appointed a sub-agent without the principal's permission, then the sub-agent performed the task in the absence of the first agent, then the first agent liked it and granted permission—still it becomes valid. The inclusion of the first agent's opinion was the principle, and that was achieved, so the sub-agent's act is valid.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This ruling extends the previous principle to a case where the sub-agent acts in the absence of the first agent. Initially, the act would be invalid because the first agent's judgment was not included at the time of the action. However, if the first agent subsequently ratifies (ijāza) the act by expressing approval or permission, the contract becomes valid. The commentary explains that the inclusion of the first agent's opinion (ra'y), which is the original purpose of the agency, is ultimately achieved through ratification. This is a Hanafi ruling that allows later approval to cure the defect of absence.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijāza): Ratification or approval by the first agent after the sub-agent's action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a sub-agent's contract become valid if done in the first agent's absence?
A) It never becomes valid
B) Only if the principal approves
C) If the first agent later ratifies it
D) If the sub-agent is a trusted person

Key Takeaway
A sub-agent's contract made in the first agent's absence is validated by the first agent's subsequent ratification.

Dismissal of Agent: Requirement of Notice
Ruling on dismissal of agent with notice requirement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dismissal of an agent and identify the three types of dismissal with their conditions.

Core Idea
Dismissal of an agent is effective only when the agent learns of it, unless the cause is automatic.

In agency (wakalah), the principal retains the right to dismiss the agent. However, to protect the agent from loss, the Hanafi school requires that the agent be notified of the dismissal. This lesson examines the general rule and its three exceptions, clarifying when knowledge is essential and when it is not.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify the ruling: the principal may dismiss the agent, but the dismissal takes effect only when the agent knows of it. Until then, the agent's actions are valid.
2
List the three types of dismissal
Categorize: 1) voluntary dismissal by principal (needs knowledge); 2) automatic due to death or loss of subject-matter (no knowledge needed); 3) principal performs the task himself (no knowledge needed).
3
Understand the rationale
Explain why knowledge is required for voluntary dismissal: to prevent the agent from suffering loss by transacting in ignorance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللموكل ان يعزل الوكيل عن الوكالة فان لم يبلغه العزل فهو على وكالته وتصرفه جائز حتى يعلم [۱۳۹۵] (۲۶) اور موکل کے لئے جائز ہے کہ وکیل کو وکالت سے معزول کر دے، پس اگر وکیل کو معزول ہونے کی خبر نہ پہنچے تو وہ اپنی وکالت پر ہے اور اس کا تصرف جائز ہے یہاں تک کہ اس کو علم ہو جائے۔ موکل نے وکیل کو وکیل بنایا ہے اور اس کا حق بھی ہے اس لئے اس کو حق بھی ہے کہ وکیل کو وکالت سے معزول کر دے۔ البتہ معزول ہونے کے لئے وکیل کو خبر ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اس لئے جب تک کہ وکیل کو اپنے معزول ہونے کی خبر نہ ہو اس وقت تک وہ وکیل رہے گا۔ اور اس درمیان اس کا خرید تا بیچنا جائز ہوگا۔ معزول تو اس لئے کر سکتا ہے کہ موکل کا حق ہے۔ اور وکیل کو علم ہونا اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ اگر اس کو علم نہ ہو تو وہ کیسے تصرف کرنے سے رکے گا، وہ تو اپنے علم کے مطابق خرید و فروخت کرتا چلا جائے گا۔ پھر اس درمیان اگر اپنا روپیہ دے دیا ہوگا تو موکل سے بھی رقم واپس لینی ہے۔ پس اگر علم کے بغیر معزول ہو جائے تو وکیل کو بلا وجہ ضر رونقصان ہوگا۔ و معزول ہونے کے تین قسم کے حالات ہیں اور تینوں کے حکم الگ الگ ہیں۔ پہلا یہ کہ موکل وکیل کو معزول کرے تو وکیل کو خبر ملے بغیر معزول نہیں ہوگا۔ دوسرا یہ کہ قدرتی حالات سے وکیل معزول ہو جائے مثلا موکل کا انتقال ہو گیا یا معین عورت سے شادی کرنے کا وکیل بنایا تھا اور وہ مرگئی تو ان قدرتی حادثات کی شکل میں وکیل خود بخود معزول ہو جائے گا۔ چاہے وکیل کو معزول ہونے کی اطلاع ہو یا نہ ہو۔ اور تیسری شکل یہ ہے کہ جس چیز کا وکیل بنایا موکل نے خود وہ کام کر لیا تو چاہے وکیل کوعلم نہ ہو پھربھی وہ معزول ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ جب وہ کام ہی نہیں رہا تو وکیل کیسے رہے گا ؟ مثلا موکل نے غلام بیچنے کا وکیل بنایا پھر اس نے خود ہی بیچ دیا یا آزاد کر دیا تو چاہے وکیل کو اس کا علم نہ ہو وکالت باطل ہو جائے گی۔ آگے کے مسئلے میں اس کی تفصیل موجود ہے۔ انوان اختیاری طور پر معزول کرے تو وکیل کو علم ہونا ضروری ہے۔
The principal may dismiss the agent from the agency; if the dismissal does not reach him, he remains on his agency and his disposal is valid until he knows. [1395] (26) And it is permissible for the principal to dismiss the agent from the agency. So if the news of dismissal does not reach the agent, he remains on his agency and his disposal is valid until he knows. The principal appointed the agent and it is his right, so he also has the right to dismiss the agent from the agency. However, for the dismissal to be effective, the agent must be informed. Therefore, as long as the agent has not received news of his dismissal, he remains an agent, and in the meantime his buying and selling are valid. He can dismiss because it is the principal's right. Knowledge is necessary for the agent because if he does not know, how will he stop transacting? He will continue buying and selling according to his knowledge. Then in the meantime, if he has spent his own money, he will need to recover it from the principal. So if he is dismissed without knowledge, the agent will suffer loss without reason. There are three types of dismissal situations, each with a different ruling: first, if the principal dismisses the agent, the agent is not dismissed without receiving news; second, if the agent is dismissed due to natural circumstances, e.g., the principal dies, or he was appointed to marry a specific woman and she dies—in these natural events, the agent is automatically dismissed whether he knows or not; third, if the principal himself performs the task for which he appointed the agent, then even if the agent does not know, he is dismissed because the task no longer exists. For example, if the principal appointed an agent to sell a slave and then sold it himself or freed it, the agency becomes void even if the agent does not know. Details follow in later issues. In summary, when the principal dismisses voluntarily, the agent's knowledge is necessary.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This is a comprehensive ruling on the dismissal (ʿazl) of an agent by the principal. The matn states that the principal has the right to dismiss the agent, but the dismissal is not effective until the agent learns of it. Until that time, the agent's actions are valid. The commentary elaborates on three distinct types of dismissal: (1) Voluntary dismissal by the principal—requires knowledge by the agent; (2) Automatic dismissal due to natural events (e.g., death of principal, death of the subject matter, apostasy and flight to enemy territory)—effective without knowledge; (3) Dismissal because the principal himself performs the task—also effective without knowledge. The underlying reasoning is to protect the agent from loss: if he is dismissed without notice, he may continue to act in good faith and incur expenses. The commentary also notes that if the principal performs the task himself, the agency ends because the subject matter no longer exists.

Key Terms
عزل (ʿazl): Dismissal of the agent by the principal from the agency.
معزول (maʿzūl): The dismissed agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Immediately when the principal decides
B) When the agent receives news of the dismissal
C) Only after a court order
D) When the agent returns the power of attorney

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, voluntary dismissal of an agent is not effective until the agent learns of it; automatic dismissals (death, loss of subject-matter, principal's own performance) take effect immediately without notice.

Agency Voided by Principal's Death or Insanity
Ruling on automatic termination of agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the events that automatically void a contract of agency (wakāla) in Hanafi fiqh and explain why no notice is required.

Core Idea
When the principal's capacity ends, the agent's mandate ends instantly.

This passage addresses a crucial question: what happens to a power of attorney when the person who granted it dies or goes insane? In Hanafi law, agency is a branch that cannot survive the root. The ruling is clear: agency ends automatically upon the principal's death, chronic insanity, or apostasy with flight to enemy territory. No notification is needed. The agent's actions after the event are void, protecting the principal's estate and third parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terminating events
List the three events mentioned: death, chronic insanity (junūn muṭbiq), and apostasy with flight to dar al-harb confirmed by a qadi.
Chronic insanity is defined as lasting one month or more.
2
Understand the legal rationale
The agent's authority (far') is derived from the principal's capacity (asl). When the principal loses legal capacity, the agency cannot continue.
3
Recognize the automatic effect
The termination is immediate and does not depend on the agent's knowledge. No notice is required.
This ensures legal certainty and prevents unauthorized acts.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a situation where the principal dies but the agent continues acting. Conclude that those acts are void regardless of the agent's awareness.
The third party buyer does not acquire ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتبطل الوكالة بموت الموكل وجنونه جنونا مطبقا [۱۳۹۶] (۲۷) وکالت باطل ہو جاتی ہے موکل کے مرنے سے ، اس کے بالکل مجنون ہو جانے سے یا مرتد ہو کر دار الحرب چلے جانے سے موکل ایسی حالت میں چلا گیا کہ وکیل بنانے کے قابل ہی نہیں رہا اس سے بھی وکالت باطل ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اس صورت میں وکیل کو معزول ہونے کی خبر ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ وہ بغیر اطلاع کے بھی معزول ہو جائے گا۔ مثلا وہ مرگیا یا مکمل طور پر پاگل ہو گیا۔ مکمل طور پر پاگل ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وہ مہینہ بھر پاگل رہا یا مرتد ہو گیا اور دار الحرب میں بھاگ گیا اور قاضی نے اس کے چلے جانے کا فیصلہ بھی کر دیا تو بغیر خبر ملے بھی وکیل کی وکالت باطل ہو جائے گی۔ شروع میں اوپر کی صورت پیش آجائے تو وکیل نہیں بنا سکتا تو اب وکالت بحال کیسے رہے گی؟ (۲) موکل ہی دنیا میں نہیں رہا تو اس کا وکیل کیسا ؟ (۳) وکیل فرع ہے اور موکل اصل ہے۔ اور اصل میں کام کرنے کی اہلیت باقی نہیں رہی تو وکیل جو فرع ہے اس میں کام کرنے کی
And the agency is voided by the death of the principal and his insanity—chronic insanity. [1396] (27) The agency becomes void by the death of the principal, his becoming completely insane, or his apostasy and fleeing to the abode of war—the principal entered a state where he is no longer capable of appointing an agent, so the agency becomes void. In this case, it is not necessary for the agent to have news of his dismissal; he is dismissed without notice. For example, he died or became completely insane. Complete insanity means he remains insane for a month, or he apostatizes and flees to dar al-harb, and the judge decides his departure, then the agent's agency becomes void without news. Initially, if the above situation occurs, he cannot appoint an agent, so how can agency remain? (2) The principal is no longer in this world, so how can his agent exist? (3) The agent is a branch and the principal is the root; when the root loses its capacity to act, the agent, which is a branch, also...
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This ruling discusses automatic termination of agency (wakāla) by events that remove the principal's legal capacity. The matn specifically mentions death (mawt) and chronic insanity (junūn muṭbiq). The commentary adds apostasy with flight to dar al-harb as another cause, and explains that in all these cases, the agency ends immediately without the need for the agent to be notified. The reason is that the principal ceases to have legal personality or capacity to contract. The commentary uses the principle that the agent is a branch (farʿ) of the principal (aṣl); when the root is gone, the branch cannot stand. The incomplete text at the end continues with this analogy.

Key Terms
جنون مطبق (junūn muṭbiq): Chronic or continuous insanity lasting one month or more, rendering the principal incapable of legal acts.
ارتداد (irtidād): Apostasy from Islam; if the principal apostatizes and flees to dar al-harb, agency ends.
دار الحرب (dār al-ḥarb): Territory under non-Muslim rule with which the Islamic state is in a state of war; flight to dar al-harb with apostasy severs legal ties.

Dismissal of the Agent and Its Effect
Ruling on principal's right to dismiss agent, with condition of notice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when an agent is considered dismissed and identify the conditions that affect the validity of the agent's actions after dismissal.

Core Idea
Dismissal of an agent requires his knowledge to take effect; without notice, his actions remain valid.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh text clarifies the principal's right to dismiss his agent and the critical condition for that dismissal to be effective. It distinguishes between voluntary dismissal, which requires the agent's knowledge, and automatic dismissal due to certain events, which does not. Understanding this nuance prevents harm to the agent who may act in good faith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Permissibility
The passage begins by stating that the principal may (mubah) dismiss the agent from the agency. This is the basic ruling: the principal has the right to terminate the agency at will.
The ruling is permissive, not obligatory.
2
Recognize the Condition for Voluntary Dismissal
The core condition: if the principal dismisses the agent voluntarily, the dismissal is not effective until the agent is informed. Until then, the agent remains an agent and his actions are valid.
The Arabic phrase 'حتى يعلم' (until he knows) is key.
3
Understand the Rationale: Preventing Harm
The commentary explains that if dismissal were effective without knowledge, the agent would continue transacting and might incur personal losses. Therefore, knowledge is required to avoid injustice.
This is based on the principle of preventing harm (darar).
4
Categorize the Three Types of Dismissal
The passage enumerates three scenarios: (1) voluntary dismissal by principal – requires knowledge; (2) automatic dismissal due to natural events (death of principal, death of subject matter) – effective immediately, no knowledge needed; (3) dismissal because principal performed the act himself – effective immediately, no knowledge needed.
These categories cover all cases of termination.

Source Text

و معزول ہونے کے تین قسم کے حالات ہیں اور تینوں کے حکم الگ الگ ہیں۔ پہلا یہ کہ موکل وکیل کو معزول کرے تو وکیل کو خبر ملے بغیر معزول نہیں ہوگا۔ دوسرا یہ کہ قدرتی حالات سے وکیل معزول ہو جائے مثلا موکل کا انتقال ہو گیا یا معین عورت سے شادی کرنے کا وکیل بنایا تھا اور وہ مرگئی تو ان قدرتی حادثات کی شکل میں وکیل خود بخود معزول ہو جائے گا۔ چاہے وکیل کو معزول ہونے کی اطلاع ہو یا نہ ہو۔ اور تیسری شکل یہ ہے کہ جس چیز کا وکیل بنایا موکل نے خود وہ کام کر لیا تو چاہے وکیل کوعلم نہ ہو پھربھی وہ معزول ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ جب وہ کام ہی نہیں رہا تو وکیل کیسے رہے گا ؟ مثلا موکل نے غلام بیچنے کا وکیل بنایا پھر اس نے خود ہی بیچ دیا یا آزاد کر دیا تو چاہے وکیل کو اس کا علم نہ ہو وکالت باطل ہو جائے گی۔ آگے کے مسئلے میں اس کی تفصیل موجود ہے۔

Book of Agency. (26) The principal may dismiss the agent from the agency. If the dismissal does not reach him, he remains on his agency and his disposition is valid until he knows. And it is permissible for the principal to dismiss the agent from the agency. So if the news of dismissal does not reach the agent, he remains on his agency and his disposition is valid until he comes to know. The principal appointed the agent and he has the right, so he also has the right to dismiss the agent from the agency. However, it is necessary for the agent to be informed of the dismissal. Therefore, as long as the agent does not know of his dismissal, he will remain an agent. And in the meantime, his buying and selling are valid. He can dismiss because it is the principal's right. And it is necessary for the agent to know because if he does not know, how will he stop transacting? He will continue buying and selling according to his knowledge. Then if he gave his own money in the meantime, he must take back the amount from the principal. So if he is dismissed without knowledge, the agent will suffer loss without cause. And there are three types of situations for dismissal, and the ruling for each is different. First: the principal dismisses the agent, then without the agent receiving news, he is not dismissed. Second: the agent is dismissed due to natural circumstances, e.g., the principal dies, or the agent was appointed for marriage to a specific woman and she dies, so in such natural incidents, the agent is automatically dismissed, whether he is informed or not. Third: the principal himself does the act for which he appointed the agent, then even if the agent does not know, he is dismissed. Because when the act no longer exists, how can the agent remain? For example, the principal appointed an agent to sell a slave, then he himself sold it or freed it, then even if the agent does not know, the agency becomes void. Details of this are in the next issue. If he dismisses voluntarily, it is necessary for the agent to know.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage states a ruling on the dismissal of an agent. It begins by affirming the principal's right to dismiss the agent from the agency. However, the dismissal is not effective until the agent is informed. Until the agent learns of the dismissal, his actions (such as buying and selling) remain valid. The rationale is to prevent harm to the agent, who may act in good faith and incur personal liability. The commentary then categorizes three types of dismissal: (1) voluntary dismissal by the principal – requires the agent's knowledge to be effective; (2) automatic dismissal due to natural events (like death of the principal or the subject matter) – effective immediately even without knowledge; (3) dismissal because the principal himself performed the act – also effective immediately. This nuanced view is consistent with Hanafi fiqh, balancing the principal's right and the agent's protection.

Key Terms
عزل (azl): Dismissal of the agent by the principal, which terminates the agency contract.
وكالة (wakalah): Contract of agency where one person appoints another to act on his behalf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, when is an agent considered effectively dismissed?
A) As soon as the principal states the dismissal in private.
B) When the agent is informed of the dismissal, even if he continues acting.
C) Only after the agent acknowledges the dismissal.
D) After a fixed period of time.

Key Takeaway
For a voluntary dismissal to take effect, the agent must be informed; his actions before knowledge are valid.

Events That Automatically Terminate Agency
Ruling on termination of agency by loss of principal's capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three events that automatically void a Hanafi agency contract and explain why the agent's knowledge is irrelevant.

Core Idea
Agency voided automatically when principal loses legal capacity — death, continuous insanity, apostasy with joining Dar al-Harb.

This passage addresses a key question in the law of agency (wakalah): when does a contract of representation end without any action from the parties? The classical Hanafi text lists three events involving the principal—death, continuous insanity, and apostasy followed by joining enemy territory—that immediately render the agent's authority void. Understanding these rules is essential for determining the validity of transactions conducted by an agent after the principal has lost legal capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three terminating events
Listen for the three specific situations: death of the principal, continuous insanity (junun muttabiq, lasting at least one month), and apostasy with departure to Dar al-Harb. These are the only events that automatically void the agency.
The text emphasizes 'muttabiq' (covering) insanity, not intermittent episodes.
2
Understand the rationale
The passage explains that the agent is a branch (far') and the principal is the root (asl). When the root loses the capacity to act (ahliyyah), the branch cannot continue. This is why the agency ends even without the agent's knowledge.
Capacity (ahliyyah) is a central concept in Hanafi jurisprudence.
3
Note the exception for public officials
The text distinguishes agents appointed by a ruler or amir: they are considered agents of the public (the ummah), not of the individual ruler. Therefore, the ruler's death does not terminate their authority, analogous to the Prophet's agents continuing after his death.
This exception preserves public interest (maslahah).
4
Distinguish between apostasy and joining Dar al-Harb
A mere apostate who has not yet reached enemy territory still has suspended capacity (mawquf). His agent is not dismissed but his transactions are also suspended. Only when he physically joins Dar al-Harb does the agency become void.
The judge's decision confirming departure is mentioned as a procedural element.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۷) وتبطل الوكالة بموت الموكل وجنونه جنونا مطبقا ولحاقه بدار الحرب مرتدا [۱۳۹۷]
۱۳۹۶] (۲۷) وکالت باطل ہو جاتی ہے موکل کے مرنے سے ، اس کے بالکل مجنون ہو جانے سے یا مرتد ہو کر دار الحرب چلے جانے سے موکل ایسی حالت میں چلا گیا کہ وکیل بنانے کے قابل ہی نہیں رہا اس سے بھی وکالت باطل ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اس صورت میں وکیل کو معزول ہونے کی خبر ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ وہ بغیر اطلاع کے بھی معزول ہو جائے گا۔ مثلاوہ مرگیا یا مکمل طور پر پاگل ہو گیا۔ مکمل طور پر پاگل ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وہ مہینہ بھر پاگل رہا یا مرتد ہو گیا اور دار الحرب میں بھاگ گیا اور قاضی نے اس کے چلے جانے کا فیصلہ بھی کر دیا تو بغیر خبر ملے بھی وکیل کی وکالت باطل ہو جائے گی۔

حاکم اور امیر کے جتنے وکیل ہیں ان کے مرنے سے وکیلوں کی وکالت ختم نہیں ہوگی وہ اپنی وکالت پر بحال رہیں گے۔ وہ اصل میں حاکم اور امیر کے وکیل نہیں ہیں بلکہ عوام کے وکیل ہیں اور وہ زندہ ہیں اس لئے ان کی وکالت باطل نہیں ہوگی (۲) حضور دنیا
سے تشریف لے گئے اور آپ کے متعین کردہ تمام وکیل اپنی اپنی جگہ پر کام کرتے رہے، کوئی آپ کی وفات سے معزول نہیں ہوا۔ وت مرتد اگر ابھی دار الحرب نہیں گیا ہے تو اس کا تصرف موقوف رہتا ہے اس لئے اس کا وکیل معزول نہیں ہوگا۔ صرف موکل کی طرح اس کا تصرف موقوف رہے گا۔
مطبق : عقل کو ڈھانک لینے والا جنون مکمل پاگل۔
(27) The agency becomes void by the death of the principal, his continuous insanity (junun muttabiq), or his apostasy joining Dar al-Harb. Agency becomes void by the death of the principal, by his complete insanity, or by his apostasy going to Dar al-Harb. The principal has entered a state where he is not fit to appoint an agent, so the agency becomes void. In this case, it is not necessary for the agent to be informed of the dismissal; he is dismissed without notice. For example, he died or became completely insane. Completely insane means he remains insane for a month. Or he apostatized and fled to Dar al-Harb, and the judge has decided on his departure; then the agent's agency becomes void even without news. At the beginning, if such a situation occurs, the agent cannot be appointed, so how can the agency continue? (2) The principal is no longer in this world, so what about his agent? (3) The agent is a branch and the principal is the root. When the root loses capacity to act, how can the branch retain capacity? It is already known that insanity and going to Dar al-Harb remove one's capacity to transact. Due to a natural incident, even if the agent does not receive news, his agency terminates. The agents of a ruler or an amir are not terminated by their death; they remain on their agency. They are not actually agents of the ruler or amir, but agents of the public, and the public is alive, so their agency is not void. (2) The Prophet (peace be upon him) left this world, but all the agents he appointed continued working in their places; none were dismissed by his death. As for an apostate, if he has not yet gone to Dar al-Harb, his transactions are suspended, so his agent is not dismissed; his transactions are suspended like the principal's. Muttabiq: insanity that covers the intellect, complete madness.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage presents the second ruling on termination of agency. It states that agency is voided automatically by three events concerning the principal: death, continuous insanity (junun muttabiq, defined as insanity lasting a month), and apostasy with joining Dar al-Harb. In all these cases, the principal loses legal capacity, so the agency ends immediately without need for notification. The commentary explains the rationale: the principal is the origin, the agent the derivative; if the origin loses capacity, the derivative cannot continue. An exception is noted for public officials like those appointed by a ruler or amir; their agency is considered for the benefit of the public and thus not terminated by the death of the appointing authority, akin to the Prophet's appointments surviving his death. The commentary also clarifies that an apostate who has not yet reached Dar al-Harb still has suspended capacity, so his agent's authority is suspended, not terminated.

Key Terms
جنون مطبق (junun muttabiq): Continuous insanity covering the intellect, defined as lasting one month without lucid intervals.
لحاقه بدار الحرب مرتدا (lahaquhu bi dar al-harb murtaddan): The apostate's act of joining the enemy territory, which renders him legally incapable of being a principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following automatically voids agency without the agent's knowledge?
A) The principal becomes mildly insane for a day.
B) The principal moves to another city.
C) The principal dies.
D) The principal becomes angry with the agent.

Key Takeaway
Three events automatically void Hanafi agency: death, continuous insanity, and apostasy with joining enemy territory — no notification needed.

Automatic Termination of Agency Upon Principal's Incapacity
Ruling on automatic termination of agency in three specific cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three events that automatically void an agency in Hanafi fiqh and explain the principle that no notification to the agent is required.

Core Idea
Agency ends automatically when the principal loses legal capacity, whether the agent knows or not.

This passage clarifies that agency is not only terminated by explicit revocation or death, but also automatically when the principal's own legal capacity to act is lost. Three specific cases are given: a mukatib slave who becomes unable to pay, a ma'dhun slave who is interdicted, and two partners who separate. In all these, the agency becomes void immediately, without need for the agent to be informed. The underlying reason is that the agent's authority depends on the principal's continuous capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage lists three distinct cases: mukatib's incapacity (عجز), ma'dhun's interdiction (حجر), and partners' separation (افتراق). Understand each: a mukatib is a slave under contract of manumission who becomes unable to pay; a ma'dhun is a slave permitted to trade who is later restricted; partners are two people who jointly appointed an agent and then separate.
These are not voluntary dismissals but changes in the principal's legal status.
2
Determine the ruling on agency
In each case, the agency is void (تبطل الوكالة) automatically. The text explicitly says 'فهذه الوجوه كلها تبطل الوكالة'.
The ruling is not simply revocation; it is an automatic voidance.
3
Analyze the condition for termination
The common element is the loss of the principal's legal capacity to be a principal. For the mukatib, once he becomes unable to pay, he reverts to full slave status and loses capacity. For the ma'dhun, interdiction removes his permission to trade. For partners, separation destroys the joint enterprise that was the basis of the agency.
Capacity is a continuing condition for agency.
4
Understand the notification principle
The text states 'علم الوكيل او لم يعلم' (whether the agent knows or not). Because the termination is involuntary and based on objective changes, no notice is required.
Contrast with voluntary revocation where notice is needed for the agency to end.
5
Derive the general maxim
The underlying principle is that agency cannot survive if the principal loses capacity. The agent's authority is derivative; if the source (principal's capacity) disappears, the agency terminates ipso facto.
This is a specific application of the general rule that agency depends on the principal's legal existence and capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۸) واذا وكل المكاتب رجلا ثم عجز او الماذون له فحجر عليه او الشريكان فافترقا فهذه الوجوه كلها تبطل الوكالة علم الوكيل او لم يعلم [۱۳۹۸]
۱۳۹۷) (۲۸) اگر مکاتب نے کسی کو وکیل بنایا پھر وہ عاجز ہو گیا یا ما ذون غلام نے وکیل بنایا پھر وہ مجور ہوگیا یا دوشریکوں نے وکیل بنایا پھر وہ دونوں جدا ہو گئے تو یہ کل و جنہیں وکالت کو باطل کر دیتی ہیں، چاہے وکیل کو علم ہو یا نہ ہو۔ مکاتب نے کسی کو وکیل بنایا پھر مکاتب اپنا مال کتابت ادا کرنے سے عاجز ہو گیا اور پھر سے غلام بن گیا تو اس کا جو وکیل تھا وہ خود بخود معزول ہو جائے گا۔ چاہے اس کو اپنے موکل کے عاجز ہونے کی خبر ہو یا نہ ہو ۔ اسی طرح غلام کو تجارت کی اجازت تھی جس کی وجہ سے اس نے وکیل بنایا تھا۔ اب اس کے مولی نے اس کو تجارت سے روک دیا اور مجبور کر دیا تو ایسا کرتے ہی غلام کے وکیل کی وکالت ختم ہو جائے گی ۔اسی طرح دو شریک تھے جنہوں نے وکیل بنایا تھا اب دونوں جدا ہو گئے جس کی وجہ سے وکیل کی وکالت ختم ہو جائے گی ۔ اس لئے کہ جب شرکت ہی نہیں رہی تو شرکت کے ماتحت عقد کیسے کریں گے؟
یہ سب قدرتی حادثات ہیں جن کی وجہ سے موکل میں عقد کرنے کی اہمیت باقی نہیں رہی اور اس بنیاد پروکیل میں اہلیت تصرف ختم ہو جائے گی اور وکالت ختم ہو جائے گی۔ اور غیر اختیاری طور پر قدرتی حادثات کی بنا پر وکیل کی وکالت ختم ہوتی ہو تو معزول ہونے کے لئے وکیل کو اطلاع ملنا ضروری نہیں ہے (۲) اس کی ایک دلیل آگے آرہی ہے جو عمر کا فیصلہ ہے۔
اصول وکیل بحال رکھنے کے لئے خود موکل میں اہلیت بحال رہنا ضروری ہے ورنہ وکالت ختم ہو جائے گی۔
(28) If a mukatib (slave under contract of manumission) appoints a man, then he becomes incapable; or a ma'dhun (slave permitted to trade) then he is interdicted; or two partners then they separate – all these cases void the agency, whether the agent knows or not. (1397) (28) If a mukatib appointed someone as agent, then he became incapable; or a ma'dhun slave appointed an agent, then he was restricted; or two partners appointed an agent, then they separated – all these void the agency, whether the agent knows or not. If a mukatib appointed an agent, then the mukatib became incapable of paying the kitabah and became a slave again, his agent is automatically dismissed, whether he is informed of the principal's incapacity or not. Similarly, a slave was permitted to trade, and due to that he appointed an agent. Then his master prevented him from trading and restricted him – as soon as that happens, the slave's agent's agency ends. Similarly, two partners appointed an agent, then they separated, so the agent's agency ends. Because when the partnership no longer exists, how can they make contracts under the partnership? These are all natural incidents due to which the principal no longer has the capacity to contract, and on that basis the agent's capacity to act ends, and the agency ends. And when agency ends due to natural incidents involuntarily, it is not necessary for the agent to receive notification of dismissal. (2) A proof of this is coming later, which is the decision of Umar. The principle: for the agent to remain, the principal must retain capacity; otherwise the agency ends.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage extends the previous rulings to specific cases: a mukatib (slave working to earn his freedom) who becomes unable to pay; a ma'dhun (slave permitted to trade) who is later restricted by the master; and two partners who separate. In each case, the principal's legal status changes such that he no longer has full capacity to be a principal, so the agency ends automatically, whether the agent knows or not. The commentary explains that these are 'natural incidents' (not voluntary dismissal) and therefore no notification is required. The underlying principle is that the agent's authority derives from the principal's capacity; if the principal's capacity is lost, the agency cannot survive. The passage also mentions that a proof from Caliph Umar will be cited later.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatib): A slave who has a contract of manumission (kitabah) with his master, paying for his freedom in installments.
مأذون له (ma'dhun lahu): A slave permitted by his master to engage in trade, having limited capacity to appoint agents.
حجر (hajr): Interdiction, restriction placed by the master (or qadi) preventing the slave from trading.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of partners who separate, the agency ends:
A) Only if the agent is informed.
B) Only if the partners had no intention to continue.
C) Automatically, whether the agent knows or not.
D) After a court order.

Key Takeaway
Agency in Hanafi law is terminated automatically by any event that deprives the principal of legal capacity, without need for the agent's notification.

Agency Terminates by Death or Insanity of Agent
Ruling on termination of agency due to agent's loss of capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two events that automatically terminate an agency contract in Hanafi fiqh and explain why they do so.

Core Idea
Agency ends automatically when the agent loses legal capacity through death or continuous insanity.

We already learned that an agency terminates if the principal dies or becomes continuously insane. The same ruling applies if the agent loses capacity. This passage mirrors that logic. Understanding this symmetrical termination helps you see that agency is a personal contract dependent on the capability of both parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is agency (wakalah). The ruling is that the agency becomes void (batil) upon two specific events.
2
List the two terminating events
The passage states: death of the agent, and continuous insanity (junun muttabiq).
3
Understand the condition 'continuous'
Only continuous insanity voids the agency; intermittent insanity does not, because the agent regains capacity during lucid intervals.
The key term 'junun muttabiq' is defined as continuous insanity covering the intellect.
4
Determine the legal consequence
The termination is automatic: no need for the principal's knowledge or a court order. Any actions by the agent after the event are void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(29) And if the agent dies or becomes continuously insane, his agency becomes void. (1398) (29) And if the agent dies or becomes completely insane, his agency becomes void.

Commentary
This brief ruling mirrors the earlier one for the principal: if the agent loses legal capacity through death or continuous insanity (junun muttabiq), the agency ends automatically. The agent is the one appointed to perform actions; if he can no longer act due to death or insanity, the agency necessarily terminates. The commentary simply reiterates the Arabic ruling.

Key Terms
جنون مطبق (junun muttabiq): Continuous insanity covering the intellect, as previously defined.

Termination of Agency Upon Principal's Incapacity
Ruling on automatic termination of agency upon principal's incapacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios in which agency terminates automatically due to the principal's loss of capacity and explain why the agent's knowledge is irrelevant.

Core Idea
Agency ends automatically when the principal loses legal capacity — the agent's knowledge is irrelevant.

This passage from the matn presents a clear ruling on the automatic termination of agency (wakalah) when the principal's capacity to act is lost. The commentator expands on three distinct scenarios: a mukatab falling into incapacity, a ma'dhun slave being restricted by his master, and two partners separating. In each case, the agency becomes void (batil) immediately, even if the agent remains unaware. Understanding this rule is essential for grasping the Hanafi principle that agency is contingent on the principal's continuing legal competence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
List the three types of principals mentioned: mukatab (slave under manumission contract), ma'dhun (slave permitted to trade), and two partners. For each, identify the event that triggers termination: incapacity, restriction, or separation.
2
Extract the underlying principle
Notice that in each case, the principal loses the legal capacity to act (due to incapacity, restriction, or dissolution). The agency depends entirely on the principal's capacity; when capacity vanishes, so does the agency.
3
Apply the rule of knowledge
The text explicitly states the termination occurs 'whether the agent knows or does not know.' Understand why: these are natural events outside the principal's control, and the agent's awareness is not a condition for the legal effect.
4
State the legal effect
The agency becomes batil from the moment of the event. Any subsequent actions by the agent are invalid. The agent is automatically dismissed.

Source Text

واذا وكل المكاتب رجلا ثم عجز او الماذون له فحجر عليه او الشريكان فافترقا فهذه الوجوه كلها تبطل الوكالة علم الوكيل او لم يعلم (مکاتب نے کسی کو وکیل بنایا پھر وہ عاجز ہو گیا یا ما ذون غلام نے وکیل بنایا پھر وہ مجور ہوگیا یا دوشریکوں نے وکیل بنایا پھر وہ دونوں جدا ہو گئے تو یہ کل و جنہیں وکالت کو باطل کر دیتی ہیں، چاہے وکیل کو علم ہو یا نہ ہو۔ مکاتب نے کسی کو وکیل بنایا پھر مکاتب اپنا مال کتابت ادا کرنے سے عاجز ہو گیا اور پھر سے غلام بن گیا تو اس کا جو وکیل تھا وہ خود بخود معزول ہو جائے گا۔ چاہے اس کو اپنے موکل کے عاجز ہونے کی خبر ہو یا نہ ہو ۔ اسی طرح غلام کو تجارت کی اجازت تھی جس کی وجہ سے اس نے وکیل بنایا تھا۔ اب اس کے مولی نے اس کو تجارت سے روک دیا اور مجبور کر دیا تو ایسا کرتے ہی غلام کے وکیل کی وکالت ختم ہو جائے گی ۔اسی طرح دو شریک تھے جنہوں نے وکیل بنایا تھا اب دونوں جدا ہو گئے جس کی وجہ سے وکیل کی وکالت ختم ہو جائے گی ۔ اس لئے کہ جب شرکت ہی نہیں رہی تو شرکت کے ماتحت عقد کیسے کریں گے؟ یہ سب قدرتی حادثات ہیں جن کی وجہ سے موکل میں عقد کرنے کی اہمیت باقی نہیں رہی اور اس بنیاد پروکیل میں اہلیت تصرف ختم ہو جائے گی اور وکالت ختم ہو جائے گی۔ اور غیر اختیاری طور پر قدرتی حادثات کی بنا پر وکیل کی وکالت ختم ہوتی ہو تو معزول ہونے کے لئے وکیل کو اطلاع ملنا ضروری نہیں ہے (۲) اس کی ایک دلیل آگے آرہی ہے جو عمر کا فیصلہ ہے۔ اصول وکیل بحال رکھنے کے لئے خود موکل میں اہلیت بحال رہنا ضروری ہے ورنہ وکالت ختم ہو جائے گی۔)
And if the mukatib appoints a man as agent, then he becomes incapable, or the ma'dhun (permitted slave) [appoints an agent] and then he is prevented, or the two partners [appoint an agent] and then they separate, then all these cases nullify the agency, whether the agent knows or does not know.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn addressing automatic termination of agency. The commentator explains three scenarios: (1) A mukatib (slave under contract of manumission) appoints an agent, then fails to pay installments and reverts to slavery; (2) A ma'dhun slave (permitted to trade) appoints an agent, then his master restricts him; (3) Two partners appoint an agent, then dissolve their partnership. In all cases, the agency terminates automatically because the principal no longer has the capacity to act. Importantly, termination occurs even if the agent is unaware. The commentator notes that these are natural events beyond the principal's control, and thus knowledge is not required for termination. The principle is: for agency to continue, the principal must retain legal capacity.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): وہ غلام جس نے اپنے آقا سے کتابت کا معاہدہ کیا ہو یعنی طے شدہ قسطوں میں اپنی آزادی کی قیمت ادا کر رہا ہو۔
ماذون (ma'dhun): وہ غلام جسے مولی نے تجارت کی اجازت دی ہو۔
شریک (sharik): شراکت میں شامل فریق، یہاں دو شرکاء مراد ہیں جنہوں نے مشترکہ طور پر وکیل بنایا۔

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mukatab appoints an agent and then fails to pay his kitabah installments, what happens to the agency?
A) The agency continues until the agent is informed.
B) The agency terminates automatically upon the mukatab's incapacity.
C) The agency is suspended until the mukatab resumes payments.
D) The agent remains but his actions are suspended.

Key Takeaway
Agency terminates automatically when the principal loses legal capacity, even without the agent's knowledge.

Termination of Agency by Death or Continuous Insanity
Ruling on agency termination due to agent's death or continuous insanity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two causes that void agency and distinguish between continuous and temporary insanity in Hanafi law.

Core Idea
Agency ends automatically when the agent dies or becomes continuously insane.

This lesson examines the conditions for a valid agency (wakalah) in the Hanafi school. The source passage addresses the effect of the agent's death or continuous insanity on the contract of agency. Understanding these conditions ensures that transactions conducted through agents remain legally binding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the first sentence of the matn: 'If the agent dies or becomes continuously insane, his agency becomes void.' This is the ruling (hukm) that agency is void (batil) under these conditions.
The ruling is unconditional upon these events.
2
Note the condition of capacity
The commentary explains that the agent must have legal capacity (being sane, adult, free). Death and continuous insanity destroy capacity, so agency automatically ends.
Capacity (ahliyyah) is required for the duration of agency.
3
Distinguish continuous vs temporary insanity
Only continuous insanity (mutbiq) voids agency. Temporary insanity of an hour or two does not void it, because capacity is temporarily absent but returns.
Mutbiq means insanity that covers the intellect with no lucid intervals.
4
Locate the proof
The commentator cites the hadith: 'When a person dies, his deeds are cut off' (Abu Dawud no. 2880). This indicates that death ends all legal capacity, including agency.
The hadith is used as a proof by analogy (qiyas) for insanity: as death removes capacity, so does continuous insanity.
5
Apply the ruling
Given any real scenario, check if the agent has died or become continuously insane. If so, the agency is void; otherwise, it remains valid. Temporary insanity does not void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا مات الوكيل او جن جنونا مطبقا بطلت وكالته (مطبق : عقل کو ڈھانک لینے والا جنون مکمل پاگل۔ وکالت بحال رہنے کے لئے وکیل میں اہلیت تصرف ہونا ضروری ہے کہ وہ عاقل بالغ اور آزاد ہو۔ لیکن جب مکمل مجنون ہو گیا تو اہلیت تصرف ختم ہوگئی یا مر گیا تو ختم ہو گیا اس لئے وکالت خود بخود باطل ہو جائے گی۔ ا یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ وکالت بحال رہنے کے لئے وکیل میں اہلیت تصرف برقرار رہنا ضروری ہے ورنہ وکالت باطل ہو جائیگی۔ گھنٹہ دو گھنٹہ کے جنون سے وکالت باطل نہیں ہوگی۔ پہلے حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ اذا مات الانسان انقطع عنه عمله (الف) (ابو داؤد شریف نمبر ۲۸۸۰) مطبق : گھیرا ہوا ہو، مکمل جنون ہو، کافی دیر تک افاقہ نہ ہوتا ہو۔)
And if the agent dies or becomes continuously insane, his agency becomes void. (مطبق means insanity that covers the intellect, complete madness. For agency to continue, the agent must be sane, adult, and free. So when he becomes completely insane, capacity ends, or when he dies, it ends; thus the agency automatically becomes void. This ruling is based on the principle that agency requires the agent's capacity; otherwise it is void. Temporary insanity of an hour or two does not void agency. A hadith has passed: 'When a person dies, his deeds are cut off' (Abu Dawud no. 2880). مطبق means enveloping, complete insanity with no intermittent lucidity.)
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn: agency ends with the agent's death or continuous insanity. The commentator explains that the agent must have legal capacity (being sane, adult, free). Continuous insanity (mutbiq) removes capacity permanently, while temporary insanity does not. The proof is the hadith 'When a person dies, his deeds are cut off,' which implies that death removes all capacity. The commentator also distinguishes between mutbiq (continuous) and temporary insanity, emphasizing that only the former voids agency.

Key Terms
مطبق (mutbiq): مکمل اور مسلسل جنون جس میں کبھی افاقہ نہ ہو، جیسے کوئی گھیر لے۔
جنون (junun): دیوانگی، عقل کا زائل ہو جانا۔

A) Any insanity, temporary or permanent.
B) Only continuous insanity (mutbiq) that covers the intellect.
C) Insanity lasting more than one day.
D) Insanity that prevents the agent from speaking.

Key Takeaway
Agency is automatically void if the agent dies or becomes continuously insane, because legal capacity is permanently lost.

Agency of an Apostate Who Joins Dar al-Harb: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on agency revival after apostasy and return

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the agency of an apostate who joins dar al-harb, explain each imam's dalil, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to a practical scenario.

Core Idea
An apostate's agency is not automatically void—Imam Muhammad suspends it, Abu Yusuf voids it completely.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about an apostate agent who joins enemy territory. While the text agrees the agent cannot act while in dar al-harb, the scholars differ on whether the agency can revive if he returns as a Muslim. Understanding this dispute illuminates how Hanafi imams apply principles of legal capacity (ahliyyah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed ruling
First, note the portion of the text upon which both imams agree: the apostate agent cannot engage in transactions while in dar al-harb.
This is the clear ruling of the matn.
2
State Imam Muhammad's view and his reasoning
Imam Muhammad holds that the agency is suspended (mawquf) and revives automatically upon return to Islam and dar al-Islam because the agent's capacity (ahliyyah) was not completely lost; only the ability to contract was temporarily hindered.
His three conditions (sanity, adulthood, freedom) remain intact.
3
State Imam Abu Yusuf's view and his reasoning
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that joining dar al-harb is analogous to death, which entirely severs legal capacity, so the agency is void (batil) and does not revive.
Thus, the principal must reappoint the agent if desired.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Muhammad, the agent's subsequent contracts are valid automatically; under Abu Yusuf, they are invalid unless reappointed.
This affects the principal's liability and the need for a new contract.
5
Note the tarjih (preferred view)
The text does not explicitly state the mufta bihi, but later Hanafi practice tends to favor Imam Muhammad's view of suspension and revival.
Consult reliable fatwa references for confirmation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان لحق بدار الحرب مرتدا لم يجز له التصرف الا ان يعود مسلما (وکیل مسلمان تھا مرتد ہو کر دار الحرب چلا گیا تو اس کی اہمیت تصرف ختم ہو گئی اس لئے وہ وکیل نہیں رہے گا۔ لیکن اگر مسلمان ہو کر واپس دار الاسلام آجائے تو کیا دوبارہ وکیل بحال ہو سکتا ہے؟ تو امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ ہاں! دوبارہ وکیل بحال ہو سکتا ہے۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ عاقل، بالغ اور آزاد ہے۔ اس لئے اس کی اہلیت تصرف مکمل ختم نہیں ہوئی تھی صرف دار الحرب جانے کی وجہ سے عقد کرنے سے عاجز تھا لیکن جب واپس دار الاسلام مسلمان ہو کر آگیا تو اب عقد کرنے سے عاجز نہیں رہا اس لئے عقد کر سکتا ہے اور وکالت بحال ہو جائے گی۔ انوں یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ مرتد کی وکالت موقوف رہے گی، مسلمان ہو کر واپس آنے پر بحال ہو جائے گی۔ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ دار الحرب جانے کی وجہ سے گویا کہ وہ مردہ ہو گیا اس لئے واپس آنے سے اس کی وکالت بحال نہیں کی سے کی ہوگی ۔ البتہ موکل نئے سرے سے وکیل بنانا چاہے تو بنا سکتا ہے۔ اصول ان کا اصول یہ ہے کہ دارالحرب جانے سے اہلیت مکمل ختم ہوگئی۔)
And if he joins the land of war as an apostate, he is not permitted to act [as agent] unless he returns as a Muslim. (The agent was Muslim, then apostatized and joined dar al-harb; his capacity for action ended, so he is no longer an agent. But if he returns to dar al-Islam as a Muslim, can his agency be revived? Imam Muhammad said yes, it can be revived. He says that he is sane, adult, and free, so his capacity was not completely lost; he was only unable to contract due to being in dar al-harb, but when he returns as a Muslim, he is no longer unable, so he can contract and the agency revives. This ruling is based on the principle that the apostate's agency is suspended and revives upon return as Muslim. Imam Abu Yusuf says that by joining dar al-harb, he is like dead, so his agency does not revive upon return; however, the principal can reappoint him if he wishes. His principle is that joining dar al-harb completely ends capacity.)
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states that an apostate agent who joins dar al-harb cannot act unless he returns as a Muslim. The commentator explains the two positions: Imam Muhammad holds that the agency is suspended and revives upon return because the agent still possesses the basic requirements (sanity, adulthood, freedom) and only the inability to contract in dar al-harb prevented action. Thus, upon return, the agency automatically revives. Imam Abu Yusuf analogizes joining dar al-harb to death; capacity is completely lost, so the agency is void and does not revive. The principal may appoint him anew. The favored position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but Imam Muhammad's view is typically relied upon in such cases of suspension.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): A Muslim who renounces Islam and adopts disbelief.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under the rule of non-Muslims with ongoing hostilities against Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The agency is void and must be renewed.
B) The agency is suspended and automatically revives upon return.
C) The agency continues uninterrupted.
D) The agent must pay compensation for missed actions.

Key Takeaway
An apostate agent who joins dar al-harb cannot act, but upon returning as a Muslim, Imam Muhammad holds agency revives automatically while Abu Yusuf holds it is void.
