Termination of Agency When Principal Acts Himself
Ruling that agency ends if the principal personally performs the delegated task

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that agency ends when the principal performs the delegated act himself, and apply it to scenarios even when the agent is unaware.

Core Idea
When the principal personally does the delegated act, the agent’s authority vanishes—whether he knows it or not.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Samari clarifies a key point in Hanafi agency law: if the principal himself carries out the task he delegated, the agency contract is automatically nullified. This rule protects the integrity of the agency by ensuring that only one person has authority over the same matter. The commentator cites the precedent of Caliph Umar to demonstrate that the agent’s knowledge is irrelevant to the termination.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the principal did (performing the delegated act) and the consequent ruling (agency is nullified).
The ruling is that the agency becomes batil (void).
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the proof cited: the athar of Umar regarding the slave-girl.
The dalil is a qawl sahabi (saying of a Companion), which is a valid source in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the athar proves the ruling: Umar upheld the emancipation (principal's act) over the sale (agent's act), showing that the principal's action supersedes the agent's authority.
The key point is that the agent's ignorance does not preserve his authority.
4
Note exceptions or conditions
Consider any conditions mentioned: the rule applies even if the agent is unaware; no exception is given for partial performance or different acts.
The ruling is unconditional as long as the principal performs the exact delegated task.
5
Apply to similar scenarios
Practice applying the rule to everyday agency situations, such as selling a car or buying property.
Think about what happens if the principal changes the subject matter (e.g., gives it away instead of selling).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن وكل رجلا بشيء ثم تصرف الموكل بنفسه فيما وكل به بطلت الوكالة (جس کام کا وکیل بنایا موکل نے خود ہی وہ کام کر لیا تو وکیل کی وکالت ختم ہو جائے گی۔ (1) جس خاص کام کا وکیل بنایا وہ کام ہی نہیں رہا تو وکیل کس چیز کا رہے گا۔ اس لئے وکالت ختم ہو جائے گی چاہے وکیل کو اس کا علم نہ ہو (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ قال قضی عمر في امة غزا مولاها وامر رجلا ببيعها ثم بدا لمولاها فاعتقها واشهد على ذلك وقد بيعت الجارية فحسبوا فاذا عتقها قبل بيعها فقضی عمر ان يقضى بعتقها ويرد ثمنها ويوخذ صداقها لما كان قد وطئها (ب) (سنن بيھقي، باب ماجاء فی الوکیل نعزل اذا عزل وان لم يعلم به، ج سادس، ص ۱۳۶ نمبر ۱۱۴۴۵) )
And whoever appoints a man as agent for something, then the principal himself acts in that matter, the agency is nullified. (The agent's agency ends because the specific task is no longer there. Even if the agent is unaware, the agency ends. Proof is the athar: Umar judged regarding a slave-girl whose master went on a campaign and ordered a man to sell her, then the master changed his mind and emancipated her and testified to that, but the girl had already been sold. They calculated, and found that her emancipation occurred before the sale, so Umar ruled that her emancipation is upheld, the price is returned, and her dower is taken because he had intercourse with her. (Bayhaqi, Sunan, باب ما جاء في الوكيل يعزل إذا عزل ولم يعلم به))
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling: if the principal performs the delegated act himself, the agency automatically terminates, even without the agent's knowledge. The commentator reasons that the specific subject matter of the agency no longer exists. The proof is the athar from Umar (radiAllahu anhu) concerning a slave-girl: the master appointed an agent to sell her, then emancipated her before the sale. When the agent sold her afterwards, Umar ruled that the emancipation took effect first, thus the sale was invalid and the price had to be returned. This illustrates that the agent's authority ended when the master himself emancipated the slave-girl, even though the agent did not know.

Key Terms
موکل (muwakkil): وہ شخص جس نے کسی کو اپنا وکیل بنایا، پرنسپل۔
وکیل (wakil): وہ شخص جسے کسی کام کے لئے وکیل بنایا گیا ہو، ایجنٹ۔

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The emancipation is invalid because the agent had authority.
B) The emancipation is upheld and the sale is void.
C) Both are valid and the agent's sale takes precedence.
D) The matter is decided by the agent's knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Agency terminates automatically when the principal performs the delegated act himself, regardless of the agent's knowledge.

Effect of Apostasy and Dar al-Harb on Agency (Wakalah): Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on apostate wakil in dar al-harb with intra-Hanafi analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a wakil who apostatizes and goes to dar al-harb, distinguish the positions of Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf, and explain the practical consequence of their disagreement.

Core Idea
An apostate agent who flees to dar al-harb loses capacity; the agency is suspended not void per Imam Muhammad but void per Abu Yusuf.

Agency (wakalah) requires continuous legal capacity in the agent. What happens when the agent apostatizes and abandons dar al-Islam for hostile territory? The Hanafi school offers two distinct views: Imam Muhammad sees the agency as suspended awaiting return, while Abu Yusuf considers it permanently annulled. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and its practical effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the initial ruling from the matn: the apostate wakil cannot act as agent unless he returns as a Muslim. This is the basis for the discussion.
2
Understand the condition for agency
Recall that agency requires ahliyyat al-tasarruf: the agent must be sane, adult, and free. Loss of capacity (insanity, death) voids agency. Here, apostasy and going to dar al-harb are examined in this light.
Complete insanity (junun mutbiq) voids agency; temporary insanity does not.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute
Identify that Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf disagree on whether the agency can revive upon the agent's return to Islam and dar al-Islam. This is the core ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze each Imam's dalil
Imam Muhammad argues that capacity is not destroyed – the agent is merely unable to contract due to being in dar al-harb. Hence agency is only suspended. Abu Yusuf analogizes to death: going to dar al-harb as a non-Muslim severs all legal ties, so agency is completely void.
Abu Yusuf's analogy relies on the hadith 'When a person dies, his deeds are cut off.'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Imam Muhammad, the agent can continue without new appointment upon return. Under Abu Yusuf, the principal must appoint him anew. This affects whether pre-existing contracts automatically resume.
The mufta bihi is not specified in this passage, but later Hanafi practice tends toward Imam Muhammad.

(۳۰) وان لحق بدار الحرب مرتدا لم يجز له التصرف الا ان يعود مسلما [ ١٤٠٠] وکالت بحال رہنے کے لئے وکیل میں اہلیت تصرف ہونا ضروری ہے کہ وہ عاقل بالغ اور آزاد ہو۔ لیکن جب مکمل مجنون ہو گیا تو اہلیت تصرف ختم ہوگئی یا مر گیا تو ختم ہو گیا اس لئے وکالت خود بخود باطل ہو جائے گی۔ ا یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ وکالت بحال رہنے کے لئے وکیل میں اہلیت تصرف برقرار رہنا ضروری ہے ورنہ وکالت باطل ہو جائیگی۔ گھنٹہ دو گھنٹہ کے جنون سے وکالت باطل نہیں ہوگی۔ پہلے حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ اذا مات الانسان انقطع عنه عمله (الف) (ابو داؤد شریف نمبر ۲۸۸۰) مطبق : گھیرا ہوا ہو، مکمل جنون ہو، کافی دیر تک افاقہ نہ ہوتا ہو۔ [۱۳۹۹) (۳۰) اگر وکیل مرتد ہو کر دار الحرب چلا جائے تو اس کے لئے وکالت کا تصرف جائز نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ وہ مسلمان ہو کر واپس آ جائے۔ وکیل مسلمان تھا مرتد ہو کر دار الحرب چلا گیا تو اس کی اہمیت تصرف ختم ہو گئی اس لئے وہ وکیل نہیں رہے گا۔ لیکن اگر مسلمان ہو کر واپس دار الاسلام آجائے تو کیا دوبارہ وکیل بحال ہو سکتا ہے؟ تو امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ ہاں! دوبارہ وکیل بحال ہو سکتا ہے۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ عاقل، بالغ اور آزاد ہے۔ اس لئے اس کی اہلیت تصرف مکمل ختم نہیں ہوئی تھی صرف دار الحرب جانے کی وجہ سے عقد کرنے سے عاجز تھا لیکن جب واپس دار الاسلام مسلمان ہو کر آگیا تو اب عقد کرنے سے عاجز نہیں رہا اس لئے عقد کر سکتا ہے اور وکالت بحال ہو جائے گی۔ انوں یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ مرتد کی وکالت موقوف رہے گی، مسلمان ہو کر واپس آنے پر بحال ہو جائے گی۔ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ دار الحرب جانے کی وجہ سے گویا کہ وہ مردہ ہو گیا اس لئے واپس آنے سے اس کی وکالت بحال نہیں کی سے کی ہوگی ۔ البتہ موکل نئے سرے سے وکیل بنانا چاہے تو بنا سکتا ہے۔ اصول ان کا اصول یہ ہے کہ دارالحرب جانے سے اہلیت مکمل ختم ہوگئی۔
(30) And if he goes to dar al-harb as an apostate, it is not permissible for him to act (as agent) unless he returns as a Muslim. [1400] For the continuance of wakalah, capacity to act in the agent is necessary: he must be sane, adult, and free. But when he becomes totally insane, his capacity ends, or if he dies, it ends; therefore the wakalah becomes void automatically. This issue is based on the principle: for wakalah to continue, the agent's capacity must remain, otherwise wakalah becomes void. Temporary insanity of an hour or two does not void wakalah. The hadith was mentioned earlier: 'When a person dies, his deeds are cut off' (Abu Dawud no. 2880). 'Mutbiq': encompassing, complete insanity with no recovery for a long time. [1399] (30) If the agent becomes an apostate and goes to dar al-harb, then acting as agent is not permissible for him unless he returns as a Muslim. The agent was Muslim; after apostasy and going to dar al-harb, his capacity ended, so he is no longer an agent. But if he returns to dar al-Islam as a Muslim, can the agency be restored? Imam Muhammad said yes, it can be restored. He says such a person is sane, adult, and free; therefore his capacity was not completely terminated, he was merely unable to contract due to being in dar al-harb. When he returns to dar al-Islam as a Muslim, he is no longer unable, so he can contract and the agency is restored. So this issue is based on the principle: the agency of an apostate is suspended; upon return as Muslim it is restored. Imam Abu Yusuf says that going to dar al-harb effectively renders him dead, so returning does not restore his agency. However, the principal may appoint him as a new agent if he wishes. Their principle: capacity is completely terminated by going to dar al-harb.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Samari deals with the effect of apostasy (riddah) and relocation to dar al-harb on the validity of wakalah (agency). The author first states the ruling: if the wakil (agent) becomes an apostate and goes to dar al-harb, he is not permitted to act as an agent unless he returns as a Muslim. The commentary then explains the general requirement for agency: the agent must have legal capacity (ahliyyat al-tasarruf), i.e., be sane, adult, and free. Complete insanity (junun mutbiq) or death terminates capacity, thereby voiding the agency automatically. Temporary insanity (e.g., one or two hours) does not void it. The hadith 'When a person dies, his deeds are cut off' supports that death removes capacity. The passage then details the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the status of the agency when the apostate returns as a Muslim. Imam Muhammad holds that the agency is suspended (mawquf) and revives upon returning as a Muslim, because the agent's capacity was not completely destroyed—only the ability to contract in dar al-harb was hindered. Abu Yusuf, however, analogizes the situation to death: going to dar al-harb as an apostate permanently ends capacity, so the agency is totally void and cannot revive. The principal must appoint a new agent if desired. The text notes the underlying principles: Imam Muhammad's view is based on the suspension of agency with the possibility of revival; Abu Yusuf's view is based on the complete termination of capacity. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is not explicitly stated here, but later Hanafi works typically follow Imam Muhammad's view in this specific case.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (dār al-ḥarb): Territory not under Islamic rule, where the agent's ability to contract is impeded.
اہلیت تصرف (ahliyyat al-taṣarruf): Legal capacity to conduct transactions; condition for valid agency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what happens to the wakalah of an apostate who goes to dar al-harb and then returns as a Muslim?
A) The wakalah is void and cannot be revived.
B) The wakalah is suspended and revives automatically upon return.
C) The wakalah continues uninterrupted.
D) The wakalah becomes void but can be renewed by verbal agreement.

Key Takeaway
The effect of apostasy and relocation to dar al-harb on agency is disputed: Imam Muhammad views it as suspended, while Abu Yusuf views it as void; the practical consequence lies in whether reappointment is required.

Principal's Own Action Voids Agency
Ruling on termination of agency by principal's act

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the principal's personal performance of the appointed task voids the agency immediately, and identify the proof from the athar of Umar.

Core Idea
A principal's personal act concerning the agency's subject matter voids the agency immediately, even without the agent's knowledge.

A contract of agency (wakalah) is built around a specific task that the agent is appointed to perform. If the principal himself performs that task, the agency loses its subject matter and is automatically voided, regardless of the agent's awareness. This lesson examines the ruling and the legal proof from the precedent of Caliph Umar (ra) recorded in Sunan al-Bayhaqi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the principal personally performing the specific task for which he appointed an agent. The ruling is that the agency becomes void (batil) immediately.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites an athar (Companion's precedent) from Umar (ra) in Sunan al-Bayhaqi (hadith 11445) regarding a slave-girl.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In the athar, the master freed the slave-girl himself after appointing an agent to sell her. Umar judged that the freeing was valid and the agent's sale was void, even though the agent was unaware. This shows that the principal's own act terminates the agent's authority.
4
Note the legal logic
The subject matter of the agency no longer exists after the principal's action, so the agency has nothing to attach to. Hence, it ceases to exist.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi status
This ruling is the established Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah) and is mufta bihi. It is not disputed within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۱) ومن وكل رجلا بشيء ثم تصرف الموكل بنفسه فيما وكل به بطلت الوكالة. جس کام کا وکیل بنایا موکل نے خود ہی وہ کام کر لیا تو وکیل کی وکالت ختم ہو جائے گی۔ (1) جس خاص کام کا وکیل بنایا وہ کام ہی نہیں رہا تو وکیل کس چیز کا رہے گا۔ اس لئے وکالت ختم ہو جائے گی چاہے وکیل کو اس کا علم نہ ہو (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ قال قضی عمر في امة غزا مولاها وامر رجلا ببيعها ثم بدا لمولاها فاعتقها واشهد على ذلك وقد بيعت الجارية فحسبوا فاذا عتقها قبل بيعها فقضى عمر ان يقضى بعتقها ويرد ثمنها ويوخذ صداقها لما كان قد وطئها (ب) (سنن بیھقی ، باب ماجاء فی الوکیل نعزل اذا عزل وان لم يعلم به، ج سادس ، ص ۱۳۶ نمبر ۱۱۴۴۵) اس اثر میں ہے للبيهقى. حاشیہ : (الف) جب انسان مر جائے تو اس کا عمل منقطع ہو جاتا ہے (ب) حضرت عمر نے ایک باندی کے بارے میں فیصلہ کیا، باندی کا مولی غزوہ کرنے گیا اور ایک آدمی کو اس کے بیچنے کا حکم دیا پھر مولی کو خیال آیا اور اس کو آزاد کر دیا اور اس پر گواہ بنایا، اور باندی کو وکیل . بیچ دیا تھا۔ پھر لوگوں نے حساب کیا تو معلوم ہوا کہ بیچنے سے پہلے آزاد کیا ہے۔ تو حضرت عمرؓ نے فیصلہ کیا اس کے آزاد ہونے کا اور اس کی قیمت واپس کرنے کا ۔ اس کا مہر لیا جائے کیوں کہ اس سے دلی کی تھی۔
(31) And whoever appoints a man as agent for something, then the principal himself acts regarding that for which he appointed him, the agency becomes void. If the principal himself does the task for which he appointed the agent, the agent's agency ends. (1) The particular task for which the agent was appointed no longer exists, so for what would the agent remain? Therefore the agency ends, even if the agent is unaware. (2) There is proof in the athar: 'Umar gave a judgment regarding a slave-girl whose master went on a military expedition and ordered a man to sell her, then the master changed his mind and freed her, and called witnesses to that. The slave-girl had been sold. They calculated and found that the freeing occurred before the sale. So Umar gave judgment that she is free, the price is to be returned, and her dower is taken because he had had intercourse with her.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: What has come about the agent being removed when he is dismissed even if he is not informed, volume 6, page 136, number 11445). This athar is from al-Bayhaqi. Footnote: (a) 'When a person dies, his deeds are cut off.' (b) 'Umar gave a judgment regarding a slave-girl: her master went on an expedition and ordered a man to sell her; then the master had an idea and freed her, and called witnesses to that; the slave-girl had been sold by the agent. Then people calculated and found that the freeing was before the sale. So 'Umar gave judgment that she is free and her price is returned, and her dower is taken because he had intercourse with her.'
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that if the principal (muwakkil) personally performs the act for which he appointed an agent (wakil), the agency (wakalah) is automatically voided. The basis is logical: the specific task for which the agency was created no longer exists as a subject of agency, so the agency has nothing to attach to. This holds true even if the agent has no knowledge of the principal's action. The text provides an athar (precedent) from Caliph Umar (ra) to support this. The story involves a master who appointed an agent to sell his slave-girl, but later freed her himself before the agent sold her. When the agent sold her unknowingly, Umar judged that the freeing was valid (coming before the sale) and the sale was invalid, so the slave-girl was free, the buyer must be refunded, and the dower (mahr) was taken because the buyer had intercourse with her. This athar illustrates that the principal's own act of freeing (which is what he had appointed the agent to sell) voided the agency, even though the agent was unaware. The footnote clarifies the hadith and the story. The underlying principle is that the agency ceases once its subject matter is removed by the principal's action.

Key Terms
وكالة (wakālah): A contract of agency where one person appoints another to act on his behalf.
اثر (athar): A narration from a Companion (here, Umar) used as legal evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, if the principal himself performs the act for which he appointed an agent, the agency becomes void:
A) Only if the agent is informed.
B) Only if the agent consents.
C) Even if the agent is unaware.
D) Only if the principal cancels the agency explicitly.

Key Takeaway
The principal's personal performance of the appointed task immediately voids the agency, even if the agent is unaware, because the subject matter of the agency no longer exists.

Agent Dealing with Close Relatives: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on agent's dealings with close relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding an agent trading with close relatives, explain their underlying principles, and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
An agent must avoid suspicion; but fair pricing may remove suspicion, allowing trade with relatives.

This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: can a wakil authorized to buy and sell transact with his own close relatives? Imam Abu Hanifa prohibits it entirely to avoid any appearance of favoritism. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) allow it but only at the market price, except when the relative is the agent's own slave or mukatab. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school balances the principles of avoiding suspicion (tuhmah) and upholding the principal's general authorization.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the parties
State the specific question: may an agent (wakil) authorized to buy/sell contract with his own close relatives? Recognize that the dispute is between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling and its basis
Abu Hanifa rules it is not permissible (la yajuz) to contract with father, grandfather, son, grandson, wife, slave, or mukatab. His reasoning is the principle of avoiding suspicion (tuhmah): a close relationship creates a strong likelihood that the agent may favor the relative.
This is based on the maxim 'ittaqū mawāḍiʿ al-tuhmah' (avoid places of suspicion).
3
State the Sahibayn's ruling and its basis
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule that the agent may sell to these relatives at the equivalent market price (mithl al-qimah). Their reasoning is that the principal's absolute authorization includes permission to transact with anyone at a fair price, and a fair price eliminates suspicion.
The exception is the agent's own slave and mukatab because their property belongs to the agent, creating self-dealing suspicion.
4
Note the exception for slave and mukatab
Both parties agree that an agent cannot transact with his own slave or mukatab. For the Sahibayn, this is because the slave's/mukatab's property is effectively the agent's own, so selling to them is like self-dealing, which still involves suspicion.
The exception highlights that even the Sahibayn block transactions where conflict of interest is inherent.
5
Determine the practical difference
A concrete scenario: an agent sells his principal's car to his father at the market price. Under Abu Hanifa, the sale is void. Under the Sahibayn, it is valid. This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۴۰۱) (۳۲) والوكيل بالبيع والشراء لا يجوز له ان يعقد عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى مع ابيه وجده وولده وولد ولده وزوجته وعبده ومكاتبه [ ۱۴۰۲] (۳۳) وقال ابو يوسف و محمد رحمهما الله تعالى يجوز بيعه منهم بمثل القيمة الا في عبده ومكاتبه. کہ مولی نے باندی کو بیچنے کا وکیل بنایا پھر خود ہی آزاد کر دیا۔ اور حساب سے معلوم ہوا کہ آزاد کرنا بیچنے سے پہلے تھا تو حضرت عمر نے باندی کے آزاد ہونے کا فیصلہ کیا اور گویا کہ موکل کے تصرف کرنے کی وجہ سے چاہے وکیل کو معلوم نہ ہو اس کی وکالت باطل ہوگئی۔ اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ جس کام کا وکیل بنایاوہ کام ہو گیا تو اب وکالت کس چیز کی رہے گی۔ ۱۴۰۱) (۳۲) بیچنے اور خریدنے کے وکیل کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ عقد کرے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اپنے باپ ، اپنے دادا ، اپنے لڑکے ، اپنے پوتے ، اپنی بیوی ، اپنے غلام اور اپنے مکاتب غلام کے ساتھ ۔ امام ابو حنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس وکیل کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ اپنے باپ، دادا، بیٹے ، پوتے ، بیوی ، غلام اور اپنے مکاتب کے ساتھ خرید و فروخت کرے۔ ان لوگوں کا رشتہ بہت قریب کا ہے۔ اس لئے موکل کو یہ شبہ ہوسکتا ہے کہ ان لوگوں سے مہنگا خریدا ہے یا سستا بیچا ہے۔ اس تہمت کی بنیاد پر ان لوگوں سے خریدنا بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اتقوا مواضع التهم۔ اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ تہمت کی جگہ سے بچنا چاہئے ۔ (۱۴۰۲] (۳۳) اور امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد نے فرمایا ان سے مثل قیمت میں بیچنا جائز ہے، مگر اپنے غلام میں اور مکاتب میں۔ امام صاحبین سے فرماتے ہیں کہ ان رشتہ داروں سے اتنی قیمت میں بیچ سکتا ہے جتنی بازار میں اس کی قیمت ہے۔ جس کو مثل قیمت کہتے [؟] ہیں۔ موکل نے مطلق بیچ کرنے کے لئے کہا ہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مثل قیمت میں کسی سے بھی بیچ خرید سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے ان رشتہ داروں سے بیچ خرید سکتا ہے۔ البتہ اپنے غلام اور مکاتب سے بیچ یا خرید نہیں سکتا۔ اس لئے کہ غلام کا مال اور مکاتب کا مال خود وکیل کا مال ہے تو گویا کہ اپنے ہی مال سے بیچا جو جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اپنے مال سے بیچنے میں تہمت ہے۔ اس لئے اپنے غلام اور مکاتب سے نہیں بیچ سکتا۔ اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ مثلی قیمت سے بیچنے میں تہمت نہیں ہے۔
[1401] (32) And the agent for sale and purchase is not permitted to contract, according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), with his father, his grandfather, his son, his grandson, his wife, his slave, and his mukatab. [1402] (33) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said: his sale to them is permissible at the equivalent price, except in the case of his slave and his mukatab. That is, the master appointed an agent to sell a slave-girl, then he himself freed her. It was calculated and found that the freeing was before the sale, so Umar gave judgment that she is free, and as if the principal's own action voided the agency even if the agent was unaware. The principle: this issue is based on the principle that when the task for which the agent was appointed is done, then what agency remains? [1401] (32) For the agent for sale and purchase, it is not permissible to contract with his father, his grandfather, his son, his grandson, his wife, his slave, and his mukatab slave, according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Abu Hanifa says it is not permissible for him to buy or sell with his father, grandfather, son, grandson, wife, slave, and mukatab. Their relationship is very close, so the principal may suspect that he bought from them at a high price or sold to them at a low price. Based on this suspicion, buying and selling from these people is not permissible. 'Avoid places of suspicion.' The principle: this issue is based on the principle that one should avoid places of suspicion. [1402] (33) And Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad said: selling to them at the equivalent price is permissible, except in the case of his slave and his mukatab. The two Imams (the Sahibayn) say that he can sell to these relatives at the price that is the market price, which is called the equivalent price (mithl al-qimah). The principal gave absolute authority to sell, meaning he can buy and sell from anyone at the equivalent price. Therefore he can buy and sell from these relatives. However, he cannot buy or sell from his slave or mukatab, because the property of the slave and the mukatab is actually the agent's own property, so it is as if he sold from his own property, which is not permissible because there is suspicion in selling one's own property. So he cannot sell to his slave or mukatab. The principle: this issue is based on the principle that selling at the equivalent price does not involve suspicion.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of an agent (wakil) who is authorized to buy and selling entering into a contract with his close relatives. The matn first states the position of Imam Abu Hanifa: the agent is not permitted to contract with his father, grandfather, son, grandson, wife, slave, or mukatab (a slave who has a contract of manumission). Abu Hanifa's reasoning is based on the principle of avoiding suspicion (tuhmah): because of the close relationship, the principal (muwakkil) might suspect that the agent favored his relative by selling too cheap or buying too expensive. The commentary quotes the principle 'ittaqū mawāḍiʿ al-tuhmah' (avoid places of suspicion). Then the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) counter: it is permissible for the agent to transact with these relatives if he does so at the market price (mithl al-qimah), except with his own slave or mukatab. Their reasoning is that absolute authorization to buy/sell implies permission to deal with anyone at the fair price, and as long as the price is fair, there is no genuine suspicion. However, the exception for slave and mukatab is because their property belongs to the agent himself; selling to them would be like selling one's own property, which would be a conflict of interest and open to suspicion. Thus, the Sahibayn's position allows the transactions subject to fair pricing, while Abu Hanifa prohibits all such transactions regardless of price. The passage then reinforces the underlying principles: Abu Hanifa's is to avoid suspicion entirely; the Sahibayn's is that fair pricing removes suspicion.

Key Terms
مثل قیمت (mithl al-qīmah): The equivalent market price; the standard value of an item in the market.
تہمت (tuhmah): Suspicion or accusation of wrongdoing; a valid reason to prohibit a transaction.
مکاتب (mukātab): A slave who has made a contract (kitabah) with his master to earn his freedom by paying installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is it not permissible for a wakil to buy or sell from his father?
A) Because the father is not a competent party.
B) Because it creates suspicion of favoritism.
C) Because the wakil cannot act for his own benefit.
D) Because the father is a mahram.

Key Takeaway
An agent's close relationship with a counterparty does not automatically invalidate a transaction; the presence of a fair market price can remove the suspicion that would otherwise prohibit it.

Agent's Sale to Relatives and Slaves: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on agent's transactions with close relatives and slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding an agent's sale to close relatives and slaves, and explain the rationale behind each view.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school divides on whether an agent may sell to close relatives: Abu Hanifa prohibits due to suspicion; Sahibayn permit at fair price.

This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: when a principal appoints an agent to sell or buy, can the agent contract with his own close relatives or slaves? Imam Abu Hanifa takes a strict position to block suspicion (tuhma), while his two disciples allow it at the fair market price, except for the agent's own slaves. Understanding this ikhtilaf reveals how the Hanafi school balances textual authorization, rational inference, and the principle of sadd al-dhara'i'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is an agent (wakīl) appointed to sell or buy (wakīl bi al-bay‘ wa al-shirā’). The dispute is whether he can transact with his father, grandfather, son, grandson, wife, slave, or mukatab.
The list of relatives is limited to those with very close ties.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling and his proof
Abu Hanifa rules it is not permissible (lā yajūz). His proof is the hadith 'ittaqū mawāḍi‘ al-tuham' (avoid places of accusation) and the principle of sadd al-dhara'i' – blocking the means to harm. The close relationship creates a strong suspicion (tuhma) of favoritism.
The suspicion is considered inherent; actual harm need not occur.
3
State the Sahibayn's ruling and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule it is permissible at the equivalent price (mithl al-qīma), except for the agent's own slave or mukatab. Their proof is the principal's absolute authorization (itlāq), which gives the agent broad discretion to sell to anyone at market price.
They argue that selling at fair price removes suspicion.
4
Analyze the exception for slaves/mukatab
Even the Sahibayn prohibit sale to the agent's own slave or mukatab because the slave's property legally belongs to the agent. Selling to them would be like selling to oneself, which is invalid due to conflict of interest.
This exception is unanimous among the three imams.
5
Determine the practical consequence and preferred view
The principal must specify restrictions if he wants to avoid such transactions. Later Hanafi practice often follows the Sahibayn for ease, but Abu Hanifa's view remains a cautionary position.
The muftā bihī may vary by region and judge.

(32) The agent for sale and purchase is not permitted to contract according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, with his father, grandfather, son, grandson, wife, slave, and mukatab. (33) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them both, said: His sale to them is permissible at the equivalent price except regarding his slave and mukatab. (Urdu commentary: The story of a master who appointed an agent to sell a slave-girl, then freed her himself. It was calculated that the freeing occurred before the sale, so Caliph Umar ruled that the slave-girl is free and that the agency was nullified because the principal's action ended the subject matter. Principle: If the task for which the agent was appointed is done, what remains for agency? (32) In Urdu: It is not permissible for the agent for sale and purchase to contract with his father, grandfather, son, grandson, wife, slave, and mukatab slave. Imam Abu Hanifa states it is not permissible because the relationship is very close, so the principal may suspect that he bought expensive or sold cheap. On the basis of this suspicion, buying and selling with them is not permissible. 'Avoid places of accusation.' Principle: This issue is based on the principle of avoiding places of accusation. (33) Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad said: Selling to them at the equivalent price is permissible, except for his slave and mukatab. They argue that the principal authorized absolute sale, meaning he can sell to anyone at the market price. Therefore, he can sell to these relatives. However, he cannot sell to his own slave or mukatab because the slave's wealth and the mukatab's wealth are considered the agent's own wealth, so it would be selling from his own property, which is not allowed due to suspicion. Principle: Selling at the equivalent price does not involve suspicion. Footnote (continuing from previous page): A man went on an expedition and ordered a person to sell a slave-girl. Then the master thought again and freed her, and made witnesses. The agent had sold her. Then people calculated and found that the freeing was before the sale. So Caliph Umar ruled that she is free, and the price should be returned. Her mahr (dower) should be taken because she had consummated marriage.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the extent of an agent's authority to transact with his own close relatives and slaves. Abu Hanifa takes a strict position: an agent appointed to sell or buy cannot contract with his father, grandfather, son, grandson, wife, slave, or mukatab. The reason is to avoid any suspicion (tuhma) that the agent may have favored his relative or himself at the expense of the principal. The principle 'ittaqū mawāḍi‘ al-tuham' (avoid places of accusation) is invoked. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) relax this rule: the agent may sell to these relatives at the fair market price (mithl al-qīma), except for his own slave and mukatab. The exception for slave and mukatab is because their property is considered the agent's own property; hence transacting with them would be like selling to oneself, which is invalid due to conflict of interest. The commentary also includes a historical anecdote illustrating a related principle: if the principal himself performs the task (freeing a slave) that the agent was appointed to do, the agency becomes void, even if the agent was unaware. The footnote mentions a case from Caliph Umar's time where a master freed a slave-girl before the agent sold her, leading to Umar's ruling that the sale was invalid and the slave-girl is free.

Key Terms
وكيل بالبيع والشراء (wakīl bi al-bay‘ wa al-shirā’): An agent appointed specifically to sell and/or buy on behalf of the principal.
مثل القيمة (mithl al-qīma): The fair market price for the item in question, without significant deviation.
تہمت (tuhma): Suspicion or accusation of wrongdoing; here specifically the suspicion that the agent acted in his own interest.

The Hanafi school splits on agent's sales to relatives: Abu Hanifa blocks it due to suspicion; Sahibayn allow it at fair price, except for the agent's own slaves.

Limits of an Agent's Purchase: Customary Price Variation
Ruling statement on the valid price range for an agent purchaser.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when an agent may purchase at a price above market value and apply the custom-based concept of yataghābanu al-nās.

Core Idea
An agent may buy at a slight customary increase, but not at an excessive price.

When you appoint someone to buy a commodity on your behalf, you entrust them with authority and also with your wealth. Islamic law balances trust and caution: the agent can pay a bit more if that is normal in the market, but if the overpayment is too large, the purchase becomes impermissible. This lesson unpacks the legal threshold of custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the act
The passage deals with a wakīl (agent) appointed to purchase. The ruling is about the validity of the contract (ʿaqd) when the price differs from the market value.
2
Distinguish permissible and impermissible price levels
Determine the three price categories: (1) exactly the market value (mithl al-qīma), (2) a slight increase that people commonly overlook (yataghābanu al-nās), and (3) an excessive increase that people do not overlook.
The decisive factor is custom (ʿurf) — what is normally accepted in similar transactions.
3
Understand the underlying rationale
The restriction is due to suspicion (tuhma) that the agent might be buying for himself at a high price and then transferring the deal to the principal. This rationale explains the exception for specific instructions.
If the principal orders a specific item, the agent can pay more because there is no self-dealing suspicion.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given a concrete case (e.g., car purchase), classify the price difference as customary or excessive based on local market practice.
Custom must be established; if uncertain, the safer course is to stick to the market price.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۴۰۴ (۳۵) والوكيل بالشراء يجوز عقده بمثل القيمة وزيادة يتغابن الناس فى مثلها ولا يجوز بما لايتغابن.

خریدنے کا وکیل جائز ہے اس کا عقد مثل قیمت سے اور اتنی زیادتی کے ساتھ جس کا لوگوں میں رواج ہو اور نہیں جائز ہے اتنی زیادتی کے ساتھ جس کا لوگوں میں رواج نہ ہو۔

خریدنے کا وکیل بنایا تھا تو اتنا زیادہ قیمت دے کر خریدنا جائز ہوگا جتنا رواج ہے کہ اس جیسی چیز میں لوگ دھوکہ کھا جاتے ہیں۔ لیکن اس سے زیادہ قیمت دے کر خریدنا جائز نہیں ہوگا۔ یہاں یہ شبہ ہے کہ وکیل نے وہ چیز اپنے لئے زیادہ قیمت میں خریدی تھی پھر اس کو موافق نہیں آئی تو وہ موکل کو حوالے کرنے لگا ہے۔ اس شبہ اور تہمت کی وجہ سے ما يتغابن الناس سے زیادہ سے خریدنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے۔

موکل نے کوئی خاص چیز خریدنے کے لئے کہا ہو تو زیادہ قیمت سے بھی خرید سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ وکیل اپنے لئے نہیں خرید سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے اپنے لئے خریدنے کی تہمت نہیں ہے۔
1404 (35) The agent for purchase: his contract is permissible at the like of the value and an increase concerning which people overlook each other in its like, and not permissible with that which they do not overlook.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This is a ruling statement for an agent appointed to purchase goods. The agent may buy at the fair market price (mithl al-qeemah) or at a price slightly higher than the market within the range that people commonly accept or 'overlook' (yutghabanu). Such a slight increase is considered tolerable in customary transactions. However, the agent cannot buy at an excessively high price that people would not normally accept. The commentator explains that the reason for this restriction is the suspicion (tuhma) that the agent might be buying for himself at a high price and then foisting the purchase onto the principal. If the principal specifically instructed the agent to buy a particular item, the agent can pay even more because there is no suspicion of self-dealing (the agent cannot buy such a specific item for himself). This ruling is a straightforward legal norm without ikhtilaf mentioned.

Key Terms
وَكِيلٌ بِالشِّرَاءِ (wakīl bi-l-shirā'i): An agent appointed to purchase a commodity on behalf of the principal.
يَتَغَابَنُ النَّاسُ (yataghābanu al-nās): A price difference that people commonly accept or overlook in similar transactions.
مِثْلُ الْقِيمَةِ (mithl al-qīma): The fair market value or equivalent price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The agent personally likes the car

C) The principal expressly allows any price
D) The agent pays the extra from his own pocket

Key Takeaway
An agent's purchase is valid at market price or a customary slight increase; excessive payment is not permitted due to suspicion of self-dealing.

Defining 'Ma La Yataghanabun al-Nas': The Price That People Cannot Overlook
Defining the term 'ma la yataghanabun al-nas'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the term 'ma la yataghanabun al-nas' and identify its objective standard based on expert valuation in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
A price outside expert valuation is one people cannot overlook—transacting at it invalidates an agent's sale.

This passage defines a critical boundary in Hanafi agency law: the line between a price that people could reasonably overlook (ma yataghanabun) and one that is so extreme that no one would normally accept it (ma la yataghanabun). Understanding this distinction is essential for determining when an agent's sale is valid or requires the principal's ratification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its core definition
The passage defines 'ma la yataghanabun al-nas' in negative terms: it is a price that does not fall within the range of expert appraisers' valuations (taqwim al-muqawwimin). Note that the definition relies on an objective, professional standard.
The term 'muqawwimin' refers to those skilled in appraising the value of goods, akin to modern certified appraisers.
2
Contrast with 'ma yataghanabun'
The commentary explains that the price range considered 'yataghanabun' (overlooked) exactly matches the range of expert valuations. Anything beyond that—higher or lower—becomes 'la yataghanabun'. Therefore, the two concepts are mutually exclusive and cover all possible prices.
3
Understand the rationale behind the definition
The passage gives a reason: 'because normally people are not deceived to that extent.' This indicates that the law presumes that parties would not willingly accept such extreme prices, so protection is needed. The standard is objective, not subjective.
This rationale links the definition to the principle of preventing exploitation (ghabn fahish).
4
Apply the definition to an agency scenario
Consider that if an agent sells a commodity at a price outside the expert valuation range, the sale is not immediately binding; it is suspended (mawquf) until the principal ratifies it. This is the practical effect of the definition.
The ruling is based on the agent's authority being limited to prices that are not grossly unfair.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۴۰۵ (۳۶) والذى لا يتغابن الناس فيه مالا يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين.

جس کا لوگوں میں رواج نہیں وہ قیمت ہے جو قیمت لگانے والوں کی قیمت لگانے میں داخل نہ ہو۔ اس عبارت میں ما لا يتغابن الناس کی تشریح کر رہے ہیں کہ جو قیمت لگانے کے ماہرین ہیں ان کی قیمت لگانا جہاں تک پہنچے وہ ما يتغابن الناس ہے۔ اور اس سے اوپر کی قیمت لا يتغابن الناس ہے۔ کیونکہ عموما لوگ اتنا دھوکہ نہیں کھاتے ہیں۔
1405 (36) And that which people do not overlook is that which does not enter under the valuation of the valuers.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage provides a definition of the term 'ma la yataghanabun al-nas' (that which people do not overlook). It is an explanatory definition, not a standalone ruling. The term refers to a price that lies outside the range of valuations made by expert appraisers (muqawwimin). In other words, if professional valuers would not even consider such a price as a possible valuation, then it is a price so extreme that people would not normally be deceived into accepting it. The commentator explains that the price range considered 'yataghanabun' (overlooked) is exactly that which falls within the range of expert valuations. Anything beyond that is 'la yataghanabun' and therefore prohibited for an agent to transact at. The underlying wisdom is that people do not commonly suffer such extreme discrepancies.

Key Terms
تَقْوِيمُ الْمُقَوِّمِينَ (taqwīmu al-muqawwimīna): The valuation made by expert appraisers; the range of prices that professionals deem reasonable for a commodity.
لَا يَتَغَابَنُ النَّاسُ (lā yataghābanu al-nās): A price that is so high or low that it falls outside the range of normal valuations and is not commonly accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, 'ma la yataghanabun al-nas' is a price that:
A) Is commonly accepted in the market
B) Is within the valuation of experts
C) Falls outside the range of expert valuation
D) Is set by the government

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, 'ma la yataghanabun al-nas' is objectively defined as any price outside the expert appraisers' valuation range, and an agent cannot bind the principal at such a price without ratification.

Agent Guaranteeing Price is Void
Ruling statement on the invalidity of agent's guarantee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that an agent's guarantee of the price from the buyer is void and explain the two reasons for its invalidity.

Core Idea
An agent for sale cannot also be guarantor: the roles of receiver and payer conflict.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling in sale agency. The agent appointed to sell cannot personally guarantee the buyer's payment. This seems practical, but the law declares the guarantee void. We will explore the reasoning based on conflict of roles and the nature of the agent's possession as a trust.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
An agent is appointed to sell an item. After selling, he guarantees the price from the buyer. Note that the guarantee is the agent's own promise, not a request from the buyer.
2
State the ruling
The guarantee is batil (void) – it has no legal effect. The agent is not liable for the price.
3
Understand the first reason: Conflict of roles
The agent's job is to receive the price from the buyer. By guaranteeing, he becomes the payer. One person cannot be both receiver and payer of the same debt; it creates a contradiction.
4
Understand the second reason: Trust vs. Guarantee
The item in the agent's possession is a trust (amanah). Guaranteeing its price effectively converts it into a guaranteed obligation, but trust and guarantee are inconsistent – one requires no liability unless negligence, the other imposes immediate liability.
5
Recognize the implications
If the buyer fails to pay, the principal cannot demand payment from the agent under this void guarantee. The agent remains only responsible as a trustee for the item until delivery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۴۰۶ (۳۷) واذا ضمن الوكيل بالبيع الثمن عن المبتاع فضمانه باطل.

اگر بیچنے کا وکیل مشتری کی جانب سے قیمت ضامن ہو جائے تو اس کا ضمان باطل ہے۔ کسی چیز کے بیچنے کا وکیل تھا اس کو بیچا اور مشتری کی جانب سے خود ہی قیمت کا ضامن بن گیا کہ میں خود قیمت دے دوں گا تو یہ ضامن بننا باطل ہے۔ وکیل وصول کرنے کا ذمہ دار تھا اور یہ خود قیمت دینے کا ذمہ دار بن گیا تو ایک ہی آدمی دینے اور لینے کا ذمہ دار بنا اس لئے یہ ذمہ داری باطل ہے (۲) وکیل کے پاس مبیع امانت کے طور پر تھی اور اس کی قیمت کا ذمہ دار بنا تو وہ ضمانت کے طور پر ہو جائے گی اور امانت اور ضمانت میں تضاد ہے اس لئے یہ ضمانت باطل ہے۔
1406 (37) And if the agent for sale guarantees the price from the buyer, his guarantee is void.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This ruling addresses a scenario where an agent appointed to sell a commodity, after selling it, personally guarantees the price to be paid by the buyer. The commentator explains two reasons for the invalidity: First, the agent's role is to receive the price from the buyer, but by guaranteeing it, he becomes both the receiver and the payer, which is contradictory. Second, the commodity in the agent's possession is a trust (amanah), but by guaranteeing the price, he effectively converts it into a guarantee, creating a conflict between trust and guarantee. Therefore, such a guarantee is void. The ruling is a straightforward prohibition without ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
ضَمَان (ḍamān): A contractual guarantee where one person assumes liability for a debt or obligation of another.
أَمَانَة (amānah): Trust; the item in the agent's possession is held as a trust, meaning he is not liable for loss unless negligent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an agent for sale guarantees the price from the buyer, the guarantee is:
A) Valid, because the agent is allowed to pay on behalf of the buyer
B) Valid, only if the principal agrees
C) Void, due to conflict between agency and guarantee
D) Void, only if the buyer is unable to pay

Key Takeaway
An agent for sale cannot guarantee the buyer's price because it creates a conflict between receiving and paying, and between trust and guarantee, rendering the guarantee void.

Selling Half a Slave by Agent: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on partial sale by agent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on an agent selling half the property and explain the Sahibayn's custom-based qualification.

Core Idea
An absolute command to sell includes selling half, but custom may restrict it to avoid harming the principal through unwanted partnership.

When a principal tells an agent 'sell my slave', does that permit the agent to sell only half? This question reveals a fundamental difference in legal interpretation. Both positions come from within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa holds the literal view, while his two disciples Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani qualify the command by customary practice ('urf). Let's walk through their reasoning and the practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the core question
Identify the exact situation: a principal appoints an agent to sell his slave, and the agent sells only half. Is that sale valid?
Note that the slave is the principal's entire property, not a share.
2
Present Abu Hanifa's position and dalil
Abu Hanifa says the sale of half is valid. His evidence: the absolute command 'sell' includes both whole and partial sale. The wording is general (amm) and covers any sale.
This is a literalist interpretation common in early Hanafi thought.
3
Present the Sahibayn's position and dalil
The Sahibayn say the sale is valid only if the agent also sells the remaining half before any dispute arises. If he cannot, the first sale is invalid because it creates co-ownership (shirkah) harming the principal. They use the principle that absolute commands are qualified by custom ('urf), citing athar from Ibrahim and Hasan about mudarib acting with ma'ruf.
Their evidence is not a direct text but a general principle of interpreting commands by custom.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If the agent sells half and never sells the rest: according to Abu Hanifa, the buyer and principal become co-owners of the slave; according to the Sahibayn, the sale is void, so the principal retains full ownership.
This difference affects the rights of the parties and the agent's liability.
5
Evaluate which view is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa)
Later Hanafi jurists (mutakhkhirin) generally prefer the Sahibayn's view because it prevents harm to the principal. Thus, the agent's partial sale without completing the whole is invalid.
This reflects the shift from strict literalism to considering custom and public interest in later Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۴۰۷ (۳۸) فاذا وكله ببيع عبده في نصفه جاز عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى.

اگر وکیل بنایا اپنے غلام کے بیچنے کا، پس اس کا آدھا بچا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ بیچنے کے حکم میں آدھا بیچنا اور پورا بیچنا دونوں شامل ہے۔ اس لئے جب بیچنے کا حکم دیا تو آدھا بھی بیچ سکتا ہے اور پورا بھی بیچ سکتا ہے۔ امام اعظم کے نزدیک مطلق لفظ دونوں کو شامل ہے۔

فائدہ: صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ آدھا بیچا اور جھگڑا سے پہلے باقی آدھا بیچا تو درست ہے۔ اور اگر باقی آدھا نہ بیچ سکا تو پہلا آدھا بیچنا درست نہیں۔ پہلا آدھا بیچا تو کہا جا سکتا ہے یہ آدھا بیچنا باقی آدھا بیچنے کا وسیلہ ہے۔ اس لئے وہ آدھا بیچنا درست ہے۔ لیکن باقی آدھا نہ بیچ سکا تو معلوم ہوا کہ پہلا آدھا بیچنا باقی آدھا بیچنے کے لئے وسیلہ نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے پہلا آدھا بیچنا جائز نہیں۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں موکل اور مشتری کے درمیان شرکت ہوگئی۔ اور صاحبین کا قاعدہ گزر چکا ہے کہ موکل کا حکم اگر چہ مطلق ہو لیکن اس کا مدار معروف پر ہوتا ہے۔ اور معروف یہ ہے کہ اس طرح بیچیں کہ شرکت کا ضرر مجھے نہ ہو۔ اور وکیل نے آدھا بیچ کر شرکت کا ضرر کیا اس لئے آدھا بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔

اصول صاحبین کا اصول گزر چکا ہے کہ مطلق حکم میں معروف طریقے کا حکم مراد ہوتا ہے۔ ان کا استدلال اس اثر سے ہے: عن إبراهيم قال: يأكل ويلبس بالمعروف. وقال الربيع عن الحسن: يأكل بالمعروف. (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب نفقة المضارب و وضيعته ج ثامن ص 247 نمبر 15083 / بخاری شریف، باب الشروط فی الوقف ص 382 نمبر 2737) اس اثر میں اگر چہ مضارب کے بارے میں ہے، لیکن صاحبین نے اسے بطور استدلال پیش کیا ہے۔
1407 (38) So if he appoints him to sell his slave, then his half (is sold), it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. If a principal appoints an agent to 'sell my slave', and the agent sells only half of the slave, Abu Hanifa rules that the sale of the half is valid. His reasoning is that the absolute command to sell includes both selling the whole and selling a part; 'sell' is general and covers partial sale. The Sahibayn qualify this: if the agent sells half and then sells the remaining half before any dispute arises, the first sale is valid because it was a means to sell the whole. But if the agent cannot sell the remaining half, the first sale is invalid because it results in co-ownership (shirkah) between the principal and the buyer, causing harm to the principal. Their principle is that even an absolute command must be interpreted according to custom ('urf), and custom dictates that sales should not cause harm through unintended partnership. They cite an athar (tradition) from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and Hasan al-Basri about the mudarib (agent in profit-sharing) eating and dressing with ma'ruf (customary manner) to support using 'urf to interpret absolute commands. The commentator notes that this is their proof.

Key Terms
شِرْكَة (shirkah): Partnership; here it refers to co-ownership between the principal and the buyer that results from selling only half the slave.
مَعْرُوف (ma'rūf): Customary or commonly accepted practice; used as a basis to restrict absolute commands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if an agent sells half of a slave and cannot sell the remainder, the sale of the half is:
A) Valid, because the command was absolute
B) Invalid, because it creates co-ownership without the principal's consent
C) Valid, only if the price was fair
D) Invalid, only if the principal explicitly forbids partial sale

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi agency, an agent's partial sale is valid only if the rest is also sold; otherwise it is invalid due to unwanted co-ownership, according to the preferred view of the Sahibayn.

Agent Buying More Meat than Instructed: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on agent's excess purchase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the binding effect of an agent's excess purchase and apply the relevant hadith to distinguish between the principal's need and expenditure.

Core Idea
The principal's need limits the agent's authority — excess quantity at the same total price is not binding without consent.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The scenario: an agent is instructed to buy 10 ratls of meat for 1 dirham, but instead buys 20 ratls of the same quality for 1 dirham. Is the principal bound to accept 20 ratls or only 10? The disagreement hinges on whether the agent's authority is defined by the principal's need (quantity) or the allocated expenditure (the dirham). We will explore both arguments, the hadith evidence cited by Abu Hanifa, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the two rulings
Understand the facts: agent instructed to buy 10 ratls at 1 dirham, but gets 20 ratls of same quality at 1 dirham. Note the two opposing rulings: Abu Hanifa says principal bound to 10 ratls for half a dirham; Sahibayn say 20 ratls for full dirham.
The price per unit has effectively halved, creating the dispute.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's reasoning (need vs expenditure)
Abu Hanifa focuses on the principal's actual need for 10 ratls. The agent's authority is limited to fulfilling that need; any excess is beyond the scope. The principal only intended to spend 1 dirham for 10 ratls, but since the market provides 10 ratls for half that, only half the price is owed.
The hadith of Urwa al-Bariqi supports looking to the principal's actual requirement.
3
Analyze Sahibayn's reasoning (authorization to spend)
The Sahibayn emphasize that the agent was authorized to spend 1 dirham on meat. The agent obtained double the quantity for the same price, which benefits the principal. The principal's instruction is interpreted broadly: buy meat with this dirham, not necessarily exactly 10 ratls.
They consider the general agency authorization and the agent's discretion to obtain the best value.
4
Examine the hadith of Urwa and its application
Abu Hanifa cites the hadith where the Prophet gave a dinar to Urwa to buy a sheep; Urwa bought two, sold one, and returned one sheep and a dinar. The Prophet approved, showing the agent should act in the principal's interest and not exceed the need. The Sahibayn may interpret the hadith differently, but the text emphasizes Abu Hanifa's reliance on it.
The hadith is a key dalil naqli for the position that the agent must consider the principal's need.
5
Determine the practical consequence and later tarjih
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Hanifa, principal gets 10 ratls for half dirham; under Sahibayn, 20 ratls for full dirham. In later Hanafi practice, the Sahibayn's view is often preferred in commercial transactions for ease of trade, but Abu Hanifa's view remains valid, especially when the principal's need is explicit.
No decisive tarjih is given in this text; both views are recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.

اگر وکیل بنایا دس رطل گوشت خریدنے کا ایک درہم کے بدلے، پس خرید لیا ہیں رطل ایک درہم کے بدلے ایسا گوشت جو بیچا جا تا ہو دس رطل ایک درہم کے بدلے تو موکل کو اس سے دس رطل لازم ہو گا آدھے درہم کے بدلے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین نے فرما یا لازم ہو گا موکل کو ہیں رطل ۔ ایک آدمی کو ایک درہم کے بدلے دس رطل گوشت خریدنے کا وکیل بنایا۔ اس نے ایسا ہی عمدہ گوشت جو ایک درہم میں دس رطل بکتا ہو ایک درہم میں میں رطل خرید لایا تو یہ میں رطل موکل کو لازم ہوگا یا آدھے درہم کے بدلے دس رطل لازم ہوگا ؟ اس بارے میں اختلاف ابوحنیفہ تھ ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی نظر اس بات کی طرف گئی کہ موکل کو صرف دس رطل گوشت کی ضرورت ہے اگر چہ اس کا خیال یہ تھا کہ دس رطل ایک درہم میں ملے گا اس لئے ایک درہم دے دیا۔ اب دس رطل آدھے درہم میں مل گیا تو آدھا ور ہم ہی لازم ہوگا اور دس رطل لیتا لازم ہوگا اس سے زیادہ نہیں۔ البتہ وہ اپنی خوشی سے لے لے تو اور بات ہے۔ ورنہ آدھا گوشت یعنی دس رطل وکیل کو لینا پڑے گا اور آدھار ہم اپنی جیب سے دینا ہوگا۔ ا امام اعظم کی نگاہ دس رطل گوشت کی طرف گئی ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عروة یعنی ابن الجعد البارقي قال اعطاه على الله النبي به دينارا يشتري به اضحية او شاة فاشترى شاتين فباع احداهما بدينار فاتاه بشاة و دينار فدعا له بالبركة في بيعه ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی المضارب يخالف ج ثانی ص۱۲۴ نمبر ۳۳۸۴ / ترمذی شریف نمبر ۱۲۵۷) اس حدیث میں ایک حاشیہ : (الف) جعد بارقی فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کو حضور نے ایک دینا ر دیا تا کہ قربانی یا بکری خرید کر لائے، پس دو بکریاں خرید کر لائے ، پس ان میں سے ایک کو ایک دینار میں یا پھر ایک بکری اور ایک دینار لے کر آئے تو آپ نے اس کی بیع میں برکت کی دعا کی۔
رطل : ایک خاص قسم کا وزن جو آدھا کیلو کا ہوتا ہے جو 442.25 گرام کا ہوتا ہے۔
The Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 2, pages 293-294. Book of Agency. (40) If he appoints him to buy ten ratls of meat for a dirham, and he buys twenty ratls for a dirham of meat of the same quality that sells ten ratls for a dirham, then ten ratls for half a dirham are binding on the principal according to Abu Hanifa, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said the twenty are binding on him. If someone appoints an agent to buy ten ratls of meat for a dirham, and he brings twenty ratls of the same fine quality that sells ten ratls for a dirham, is he bound to take twenty for the dirham or ten for half a dirham? There is a dispute. Abu Hanifa looks to the need: the principal only needs ten ratls; he gave a dirham thinking ten ratls cost that much. Now that ten ratls appear for half a dirham, only half the dirham is spent, so ten ratls are binding, not more. If he wishes, he may take more, but otherwise twenty ratls are not binding. The agent must receive ten ratls and pay half a dirham. Abu Hanifa's proof is the hadith of Urwa ibn al-Ja'd al-Bariqi: the Prophet gave him a dinar to buy a sacrificial animal or a sheep; he bought two sheep and sold one for a dinar, then came with a sheep and a dinar, and the Prophet prayed for blessing in his sale. (Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi). A note: Al-Bariqi says the Prophet gave him a dinar to buy a sacrificial animal, so he bought two, then sold one for a dinar and brought one sheep and one dinar, and the Prophet prayed for blessing. Ratl: a specific weight equal to half a kilo or 442.25 grams.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), regarding an agent who purchases more than instructed at the same total price. Abu Hanifa focuses on the principal's actual need (ten ratls) and concludes that only ten ratls are binding at the reduced cost of half a dirham; the agent must bear the extra cost of the other ten ratls. The Sahibayn focus on the agent's authority to spend the entire dirham and thus hold the principal bound to accept all twenty ratls for the full dirham. Abu Hanifa supports his view with the hadith of Urwa al-Bariqi, where the agent (Urwa) bought two animals with the principal's money but returned only one animal and the change, and the Prophet approved. This shows that the agent should act in the principal's interest. The Sahibayn, however, consider the general authorization to buy meat for a dirham and argue that the principal is bound by the agent's discretion to obtain the best value. The term 'ratl' is clarified as a weight of about 442.25 grams.

Key Terms
رطل (ratl): A unit of weight, approximately 442.25 grams or half a kilogram, used for meat.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two disciples of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
قبض (qabd): Possession or taking delivery of the purchased item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 20 ratls for 1 dirham
B) 10 ratls for half a dirham
C) 10 ratls for 1 dirham
D) 20 ratls for half a dirham

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi agency, the principal's actual need may limit the agent's authority, even if the agent obtains a better deal.

Agent Cannot Buy a Specific Thing for Himself
Ruling on agent buying a specific item for himself

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an agent is appointed to buy a specific item and identify the reason for the prohibition.

Core Idea
An agent entrusted to buy a specific item cannot buy it for himself — it is a breach of trust.

This lesson addresses a key principle in the law of agency (wakalah). When a principal appoints an agent to purchase a specific, identifiable item (shay' bi-'aynihi), a special trust is created. The agent must act solely for the principal's benefit. Buying that identical item for himself violates that trust and is legally prohibited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is an agent buying a specific item he was appointed to purchase for the principal. The ruling is: not permissible (prohibited).
The ruling is clear — 'la yajuz' meaning it is not allowed.
2
Understand the reason (علة)
The reason is the principal's trust (i'timad) and the deception (khayanah) involved if the agent buys for himself.
The Arabic term used is 'خيانة' (khayanah) — a breach of trust.
3
Distinguish from generic items
This rule applies only when the item is specified ('ayn), not when the agent is asked to buy a generic item (e.g., 'buy a car'). For generic items, the agent may buy a similar item for himself as long as he fulfills the principal's order.
This distinction is crucial in Hanafi agency law.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider: Principal says, 'Buy that specific house at 123 Main St.' Agent purchases it for himself. The contract is invalid for the principal, and the agent must compensate or give the property to the principal.
The agent's purchase for himself is not recognized — the principal has a right to claim the property.

Source Text

[١٤١٠] (٤١) وان وكله بشراء شيء بعينه فليس له ان يشتريه لنفسه 
اور اس کی تفسیر: اگر کسی متعین چیز کے خریدنے کا وکیل بنایا تو اس کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ اس کو اپنے لئے خریدے۔ موکل نے اس پر اعتماد کیا ہے کہ میرے لئے خریدے گا اور وکیل نے اپنے لئے خرید لیا تو اس میں ایک قسم کا دھوکہ دیتا ہوا ۔ اس لئے وکیل متعین چیز کو اپنے لئے نہیں خرید سکتا۔
(41) If he appoints him to buy a specific thing, it is not permissible for him to buy it for himself. Explanation: If someone is appointed to buy a specific thing, it is not permissible for him to buy it for himself. The principal relies on him to buy for him, and if the agent buys it for himself, there is deception involved. Therefore, the agent cannot buy the specific thing for himself.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a straightforward ruling: when an agent is appointed to purchase a specific item (shay' bi-'aynih), he may not buy that item for himself. The reason is that such an act constitutes a breach of trust (khayanah) and deception (ghishsh), as the principal appointed him specifically to secure that identical item. The agent is obligated to act solely for the principal's benefit.

Key Terms
شيء بعينه (shay' bi-'aynihi): A specific, identifiable thing (as opposed to a generic item).
وكالة (wakalah): Agency; a contract where one appoints another to act on his behalf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
An agent is appointed to buy a specific painting. Can the agent buy that painting for himself?
A) Yes, if he pays the same price
B) No, it is a breach of trust
C) Yes, with the principal's permission
D) Only if the painting is not available for the principal

Key Takeaway
An agent appointed to buy a specific item must buy it only for the principal; self-purchase is prohibited as a breach of trust.

Agent Buying a Non-Specific Slave
Ruling on agent buying a generic slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default ownership rule when an agent buys a non-specific item and identify the conditions that transfer ownership to the principal.

Core Idea
A generic purchase by an agent belongs to the agent unless he intends otherwise or uses the principal's funds.

In this passage, we learn the default rule for an agent who buys a non-specific slave (or any generic item). Since the agent is not told which specific slave to buy, there is ambiguity about whom the agent was acting for. The Hanafi school applies a clear presumption: the purchase is for the agent unless there is a clear indication of intent to buy for the principal. This lesson unpacks that rule and its underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Understand that the agent is appointed to buy a slave without specifying a particular individual (bighayri aynihi). This creates ambiguity about whose behalf the agent is buying.
The item is described generally, not identified specifically.
2
State the default ruling
The purchased slave belongs to the agent by default, because people normally buy for themselves.
This is the presumptive rule (asl).
3
Identify the exceptions
If the agent explicitly states 'I intended to buy for the principal' (nawaytu lilmuwakkil) or uses the principal's money to buy, then the slave belongs to the principal.
These are indicators (qarina) that override the default.
4
Understand the rationale
The default is based on the norm that a person acts for their own interest. Exceptions require clear evidence of contrary intent.
This aligns with the Hanafi principle that actions are judged by intentions.
5
Apply the principle
The same rule applies to any generic item (e.g., horse, car) purchased by an agent, not just slaves.
The ruling is general (amm) in its application.

[١٤١١] (٤٢) وان وكله بشراء عبد بغير عينه فاشترى عبدا فهو للوكيل الا ان يقول نويت الشراء للموكل او يشتريه بمال الموكل 
اور اس کی تفسیر: اور اگر کسی غیر متعین غلام کو خریدنے کا وکیل بنایا، پس اس نے غلام خریدا تو وکیل کے لئے ہوگا، مگر یہ کہ کہے میں نے موکل کے لئے خریدنے کی نیت کی تھی یا اس کو موکل کے مال سے خریدے۔ غیر متعین غلام خریدنے کا وکیل بنایا تھا۔ ایسی صورت میں ایک غلام خریدا تو جب کوئی ایسی علامت نہ ہو کہ یہ موکل کے لئے خریدا ہے اس وقت تک وہ غلام وکیل کے لئے ہی شمار کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ عموما آدمی اپنے لئے ہی خریدتا ہے۔ موکل کے لئے خریدنے کی علامت میں سے یہ ہے کہ خریدتے وقت موکل کی نیت کرے یا کم از کم موکل کے مال سے غلام خریدے تو وہ غلام موکل کے لئے ہوگا۔ اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ موکل کے لئے خریدنے کی علامت ہو تو موکل کے لئے ہوگا ورنہ اپنی ذات کے لئے ہوگا۔
(42) If he appoints him to buy a slave not by specification, and he buys a slave, it is for the agent unless he says 'I intended to buy for the principal' or he buys it with the principal's money. Explanation: If someone is appointed to buy a non-specific slave and he buys a slave, it belongs to the agent, unless he says he intended to buy for the principal or he buys it with the principal's money. When there is no indication that it is for the principal, it is considered for the agent, because a person normally buys for himself. Indicators of buying for the principal include intending at the time of purchase or using the principal's money. The principle is: if there is an indication, it is for the principal; otherwise for the agent.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage provides the default rule for an agent purchasing a generic (non-specific) item. Since the item is not identified, there is an ambiguity about whose behalf the agent acted. The default presumption is that the agent bought for himself, because people typically buy for themselves. However, if the agent explicitly states his intention (niyyah) to buy for the principal, or if he uses the principal's money to make the purchase, then the item belongs to the principal. This aligns with the Hanafi principle that actions are judged by intentions.

Key Terms
نويت (nawaytu): I intended; the agent's declaration of intent to buy for the principal.
بغير عينه (bi-ghayri 'aynihi): Without specification; a generic description rather than a specific individual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
An agent is appointed to buy any suitable horse. He buys a horse with his own money and does not state his intention. Who owns the horse?
A) The principal
B) The agent
C) Both
D) The seller

Key Takeaway
In a generic agency purchase, the agent is the presumed owner unless there is evidence of intent for the principal.
